Inauguration Ceremony of Members of Jiangsu Provincial Government 76

The newly appointed members of the Jiangsu Provincial Government held a swearing-in ceremony at 9:30 AM this morning (the 1st) in the auditorium of the Provincial Government. Those present included the Chairman of the Provincial Government Ye Chucang, members Hu Pu'an, Chen Qicai, Chen Hexian, Sun Hongzhe, He Yushu, Li Mingyang, Luo Liangjian, Wang Chonghui representing the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government, Tao Gongheng representing the Executive Yuan, Xu Dongfan and Fan Guang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Jin Baoshan of the Ministry of Health, Bi Jingqian of the Auditing Yuan, Zhang Quan and Ren Jiaqi of the Garrison Headquarters, Enkebaatu of the Legislative Yuan, Dong Xiangrui of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, Chen Dasan of the Ministry of Interior, Xu Pucheng of the Zhejiang Water Police, Zhang Daofan, Ye Xiufeng, and Zhang Yuanyang of the Provincial Party Consolidation Committee, representatives of various institutions and organizations, and staff members of the Provincial Government's departments, totaling about a thousand people. After the meeting and salute, Wang Chonghui, representing the National Government, presented the seal and delivered an instruction, which stated, "Jiangsu occupies a special position in China's geography. Politics, culture, and financial resources are all the best in the country. Chairman Ye and the members take office today. I will say two things on behalf of the colleagues in the Central Government. Now, political and social physiologists use a person's physiological proportions to describe the position of politics. The center is the head of the person, the provincial government is the abdomen of the person, and the counties are the limbs of the person. The head must rely on the body to introduce the brain's command of the limbs. There has never been a case where the abdomen is not healthy but the head can clearly command the limbs as desired. Therefore, the center is to the counties, and the provincial government will be the pivot to make the administration as desired. Chairman Ye has a history of revolutionary struggle and experience. In the future, he will be able to popularize Jiangsu's counties in accordance with the central government's general principles for finance, education, transportation construction, etc. The benefit of Jiangsu is the blessing of the world. I wish you all good health on behalf of my colleagues in the Central Government." Next, Tao Gongheng, representing the Executive Yuan, delivered a speech, which stated, "The new Director of Finance, Member Chen, once served in Zhejiang as the Director of Finance. He is good at managing finances and is honest. Director Hu is a Chinese scholar. He is coming to serve in civil affairs. The other new and old directors of departments and provincial members are all virtuous officials with outstanding achievements. Chairman Ye has expressed to the Executive Yuan in Beijing that the first problem in Jiangsu's political facilities is bandit suppression. Now there are many bandits in the four townships, the wealthy live in Shanghai, and the less wealthy live in the city. There is no one in the township government, and financial resources will be exhausted. Chairman Ye has the determination to suppress bandits, which is not only a blessing for Jiangsu Province, but also a good model for the central government to command other provinces." Then, representatives of the Ministry of Interior and Ministry of Foreign Affairs and representatives of the Provincial Party Headquarters delivered speeches. Finally, Chairman Ye Chucang replied, "Today, I am very honored to receive the encouragement from the swearing-in officer and the representatives. The more hope there is, the more uneasy I feel. We are ordered by the central government to do things for the people of Jiangsu. We feel that we are here to do things, not to be officials like in the past bureaucratic era. Therefore, we must now fulfill our obligations, not enjoy our rights. It is our duty to fulfill our obligations and do well. If there is no achievement, then we have not fulfilled our obligations. We only feel that we dare not take credit. If there are any mistakes or omissions, it is our fault. We are always uneasy and have no time to be happy. Perhaps this uneasiness will reduce negligence and mistakes. I hope that the central government and all sectors will often encourage us." After the speech, the ceremony was completed and the meeting was adjourned.

The Yellow River in Shandong Province is in Extreme Danger 77

Jinan Correspondence: The Yellow River in this province has just passed the ice run stage, and the peach blossom floods are about to arrive. The downstream areas are in extreme danger. The most critical issue is the dike closure project at Hujiatan in Lijin downstream. This breach occurred in February of last year. Last summer, Provincial Government Commissioner Yan Rongde went to close the breach, spending 300,000 yuan, but the more they tried to close it, the larger the breach became. Generally, river works are most afraid of closing breaches during high water; nine out of ten attempts fail. It is not fair to blame Mr. Yan alone. In winter, when the water receded, the breach was only two or three feet deep. The River Affairs Bureau estimated that the cost of closing the breach would be 70,000 yuan, which could be easily accomplished. However, the Finance Department has only allocated 30,000 yuan to date, and both funds and materials are lacking, leaving them helpless. Therefore, during the ice run, the breach was further enlarged by ice floes. Originally, only 20% of the water flowed through the breach, but now 60% flows through it, with a depth of twelve feet, taking nearly two-thirds of the main current. The River Affairs Bureau has estimated the cost for a second time, requiring 119,000 yuan to close the breach, but the Finance Department has not yet allocated the funds, so work cannot begin. In the blink of an eye, the peach blossom floods will rise again, and there is fear of repeating last year's failures, making it impossible to close the breach. This is the dangerous situation of the Hu dike project. Furthermore, according to the River Affairs Bureau's usual practice, during the spring low water, the entire river's dikes and dams are repaired to prevent floods and breaches, known as "Spring Repairs." This is not only precautionary but also achieves twice the results with half the effort. In the seventeenth year, Zhang Zongchang was defeated and fled, followed by the Jinan Incident. In the spring of the eighteenth year, the Jinan Incident was not yet resolved, and the Provincial Government had not yet moved to Jinan, resulting in the complete neglect of Spring Repair projects for two years. All the river's dikes are riddled with holes, causing dangerous conditions. The River Affairs Bureau has repeatedly appealed, but the funds for Spring Repairs have not yet been issued. Four representatives of the disaster victims in Lijin came to Jinan the day before yesterday to petition the Provincial Government, Finance Department, and River Affairs Bureau, detailing the dangerous situation downstream. Yesterday, the Provincial Government Standing Committee approved the River Works Committee to review the funds for closing the breach at Hujiatan and the funds for repairing Spring Repairs. After review, the Finance Department will allocate funds to close the breach. However, although the River Works Committee is the superior authority of the River Affairs Bureau, it has not held a meeting for several weeks. If it is necessary to wait for the committee to meet and approve, or to re-estimate the project at Hujiatan, before issuing funds, then the time will be too long, and the water will not wait. The people of several downstream counties will truly suffer the disaster of being fish. (28th)

The Shanxi Provincial and Municipal Party Headquarters are Sealed 78

The Minguo Daily and Jinxin Bookstore are also Searched

Taiyuan Correspondence: The Shanxi Provincial and Municipal Party Headquarters and the Minguo Daily office were searched by a joint force of military police and constabulary around 5 PM the day before yesterday (the 22nd). According to official statements, the reason for this action was that there were abnormal activities within the Party Headquarters. However, according to my understanding, it was due to the discovery of a large number of propaganda materials in the city the day before, containing absurd and outrageous mentions of Yan Xishan and others. The authorities believed that these materials were produced by the Party Headquarters, hence this action. The search of the Provincial Party Headquarters, Municipal Party Headquarters, Minguo Daily office, and Jinxin Bookstore, which prints the Minguo Daily, was carried out simultaneously. The Provincial Party Headquarters was guarded by a battalion of garrison soldiers and many police and constables. The other locations each had between forty and fifty or more than a hundred personnel, armed with live ammunition, assisting in the operation. The supervisors and committee members of the Provincial Party Headquarters had either gone to Beijing beforehand or had gone into hiding, leaving only a few staff members inside. The department's disciplinary team initially closed the main gate, intending to refuse the inspection. However, the garrison soldiers moved several machine guns and aimed them at the Party Headquarters' gate, with boxes of ammunition. Seeing the unfavorable situation, the disciplinary team agreed to disarm themselves, collect the weapons, and then open the gate. Immediately afterward, they left empty-handed. The military police and constables outside entered the Party Headquarters and immediately began surveillance. At the Municipal Party Headquarters, there were no complications. The military police allowed all staff members to take their luggage and move out that evening. All documents and equipment were temporarily guarded by the military police. The search of Jinxin Bookstore was quite strict, with the entire area surrounded, cutting off all internal and external communication. All propaganda materials were temporarily placed in one location. At the Minguo Daily office, only editor Wang Ying, a Mr. Lan, and business manager Dong Jingru were present at the time. The others had not yet arrived because it was still early. The publication was suspended from that evening. Around 5 PM yesterday, the General Headquarters and Special Party Headquarters dispatched Wang Gaisen, Liu Hanlin, Xia Guozhen, and three others to take over the Provincial Party Headquarters, Municipal Party Headquarters, and Minguo Daily, respectively, sealing and securing all documents and items. The detained personnel were also released. However, soldiers continued to guard the four locations. As for the branch offices and joint offices of various cities, counties, and districts, they have already erected signs at No. 3 Haizi Edge and have begun operations. The association and the Special Party Headquarters have been unusually active in recent days. The aftermath of the Provincial and Municipal Party Headquarters will be resolved at the citizens' assembly. Recently, students from various schools have organized revolutionary youth groups, and slogans are posted all over the streets, with leaflets flying like snowflakes, seemingly ending the previous period of silence. (March 24th)

Zhu and Mao Flee and Disrupt the Guangdong Border 79

Nankang and Dagan on the Jiangxi Border Have Been Occupied by Bandits

Guangdong Training Regiment Heads to Nanxiong for Defense

Guangzhou Correspondence: The remnants of the Communist bandits Zhu and Mao in southern Jiangxi have recently taken advantage of the local emptiness to harass in all directions. They previously attacked Ganzhou and were repelled by the Jiangxi army. One group of Communist bandits fled to Shangyou, and another group fled south again, passing through Nankang, with the intention of crossing the Dagan Mountains and eyeing Nanxiong in northern Guangdong. Because Nankang County had no defending troops, the bandits were able to drive straight in. It is reported that on the 20th, Nankang fell to the bandits, and the bandits took the opportunity to invade south, taking the route of Xincheng, Chijiangwei, and Qinglongwei, directly to Nan'an (i.e., Dagan County). Nanxiong in Guangdong is only one hundred and twenty li from Dagan. Local organizations and groups in that area have been sending urgent telegrams for days. (1) The Nanxiong Chamber of Commerce telegraphed, saying that Zhu and Mao's large forces have successively captured counties on the Jiangxi border and are approaching Nanxiong. Jiangxi Province has dispatched troops to pursue and suppress them. The bandits have nowhere to retreat and will inevitably flee to Nanxiong. They request immediate dispatch of troops to assist them day and night, and kindly request a telegraphic reply. (2) The magistrate of Shixing County telegraphed, stating that according to reports, Communist bandits are fleeing to Nan'an, eyeing Nanxiong. The county is preparing to meet them. They request assistance. (3) The magistrate of Nanxiong County telegraphed, saying that according to confirmed reports, Zhu De's Communist bandits set out from Nankang in two routes, one from Shangyou and Chongyi, and the other from the main road. It is said that they have arrived at Xincheng and are fleeing towards Dagan. It is found that Xincheng is only sixty li from the Guangdong border, and there are no troops to defend along the way. Nanxiong is in extreme danger. He urgently requests the prompt urging of the 63rd Division's training regiment to assist day and night. Nanxiong County Magistrate Mei Yiqiang bows and begs. After receiving repeated urgent telegrams, the authorities have received further warnings, stating that Dagan and Xinfeng counties were captured by bandits on the 23rd, with the intention of crossing the Dagan Mountains and entering Nanxiong in Guangdong Province. Businesses in Nanxiong have sent telegrams to Shaoguan and Guangzhou, stopping the dispatch of goods. Wealthy residents of Nanxiong City are even moving their families. Yesterday, the authorities have transferred Wu Wenxian, the chief of staff of the 63rd Division, to lead the division's new recruits training regiment to Nanxiong to coordinate with the local military police to strictly defend. (March 26th)

Communist Bandits in Western Fujian Flee and Capture Yongfu 80

The Newly Organized First Division Has Sent Troops to Suppress Them

Xiamen Correspondence: The local Communist bandits in western Fujian recently concentrated in Longyan, led by Communist leader Deng Zihui. On the 22nd, they captured Hexi. The local Communist bandits stationed in Baihe, led by Fu Bocui, attacked Xiepu camp on the 22nd. After the Baihe militia led by Zhan Jifu and the Fifth Security Brigade led by Liu Liebo resisted with all their might, the Communist bandits retreated to Baisha in the evening. On the morning of the 23rd, Deng Zihui led about 2,000 Communist bandits from Hexi and Baisha towards Yongfu, which belongs to Zhangping County. At dawn on the 24th, they suddenly attacked Yongfu. The garrison only had 200 soldiers of the Security Brigade under Xiao Jiwu. They were caught off guard and vastly outnumbered. Xiao's troops were disarmed of over a hundred, and Xiao was also captured. Yongfu was thus captured. Xiao was subsequently burned to death by the Communist bandits. Yongfu is only eighty li from Zhangping County. After the Communist bandits entered the town, they looted and levied funds. Most of those with some assets fled. On the 25th, Deng sent over a hundred Communist bandits to occupy Guantian, which is twenty li from Hua'an County, and cut off the telegraph lines. When the Communist bandits captured Hexi, the Newly Organized First Division of Zhangzhou immediately sent a battalion of troops to join the soldier battalion and security team of Jinshan to recover Hexi on the 24th. On the 25th, they transferred two battalions of Chen Linrong's Third Regiment to advance towards Nan'an to suppress the Communist bandits in Hexi and to attack Yongfu from the rear. They also transferred all of Huang Kesheng's Fourth Regiment to advance towards Zhangping via Punan. It is said that one part of Huang's regiment has already set out, and the advance troops have arrived in Hua'an. This route is the main force for suppressing the Communist bandits in Yongfu. With such strong forces on both routes, it should not be difficult to eliminate them. On the 27th, Yang Fengnian, the Second Brigade Commander of the First Division, Lin Xuezeng, the Magistrate of Longxi County, and Zhu Peihuang, the director of the Longxi 指委, convened a joint meeting of party, government, and military representatives at the county party headquarters to discuss the prevention and suppression of bandits and the maintenance of public order. Zhangzhou has been under martial law since the 25th. (March 28th)

The Longhai Railway Bureau Moves from Zhengzhou to Xuzhou 81

Xuzhou Correspondence: Qian Zongze, the director of the Longhai Railway Bureau, after going to Zhengzhou to take over the bureau, went to Beijing to report to the Ministry of Railways. The bureau originally intended to remain in Zhengzhou and not move, to avoid confusion. However, due to changes in the situation in the Northwest, the Bianzheng trains have been interrupted. After Qian returned to Xuzhou from Zhengzhou this time, he immediately requested and received approval from the Ministry of Railways to temporarily move the Longhai Railway Bureau to Xuzhou for convenience. The personnel from the Zhengzhou bureau have already come to Xuzhou separately. The newly appointed officials in Xuzhou have also arrived at the bureau. The bureau is located at the Longhai North Station. Qian appointed Yan Zuolin as the chief secretary, and he began working on March 27th. The bureau is divided into five departments: General Affairs, Accounting, Transportation, Mechanical Engineering, and Civil Engineering. Yu Shibin is the director of the General Affairs Department, which includes the Document Section, headed by Yi Weicheng; the Translation Section, headed by Lu Dezheng; the General Affairs Section, headed by Qian Ziyuan; and the Materials Section and Police Section, for which the heads have not yet been determined. The Mechanical Engineering Department is temporarily headed by Chief Engineer Lin Yi, and the Civil Engineering Department is temporarily headed by Chief Engineer He Xianhua. The director of the Transportation Department, a French national, is still in Zhengzhou and has not yet arrived. Huang Zhaoxiang has been appointed as the deputy director. The head of the Accounting Department has also not been determined. It is said that they must be recommended by the French and Belgian banking groups. Each department is further divided into sections, which are currently being organized and established.

Twists and Turns in the Future of the Sino-Soviet Conference 82

Mo Dehui Will Have Difficulty Departing on the 10th

Soviet Russian Personnel Do Not Discuss This Matter

Harbin Correspondence, March 24th: It was rumored a few days ago that Mo Dehui had telegraphed the central government, stating that he was scheduled to go to Russia on April 10th and convene the Sino-Soviet conference in Moscow on the 15th. Regarding this matter, I visited relevant parties today, who claimed that this was not the case, and Mr. Mo had not telegraphed the central government regarding a firm departure date. It is also heard that the true intentions of Soviet Russia have not yet been clearly expressed. Even the director of the Russian consulate and the Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau in Harbin does not discuss this matter. Therefore, the Russian attitude towards the conference is difficult to grasp. If their consent is not obtained in advance, there is no reason to go rashly. As Mo Dehui is in a position of full authority, he should not directly express any opinions to the Russian side, lest the Russian side develop a sense of contempt. Therefore, it is necessary for the newly appointed special envoy for diplomacy in Harbin, Zhong Yu, to formally notify Russia after his arrival, and only after obtaining a reply from the Russian side agreeing to it, can Mr. Mo set out. However, Zhong Yu sent a letter to his friend in Harbin yesterday, stating that due to discussing matters with Chairman Zhang (Zuoxiang), he would need to come to Harbin at the end of the month to take office. Only after Zhong arrives in Harbin at the end of the month to negotiate with Russia and everything is in order, will Mr. Mo be able to depart in half a month. Therefore, Mr. Mo's originally scheduled departure on April 10th will likely be postponed again. Of the two attendants assigned by the central government, except for Tu Wei Zeng, who has already arrived in Harbin, Li Chen is still in Hangzhou. Due to these various issues, Mr. Mo's trip to Russia will not be easy to realize in the short term. It is vaguely heard that key Russian figures in Harbin have indicated to third parties that the Soviet Russian side has not received the Nanjing Ministry of Foreign Affairs' declaration on the Sino-Soviet conference. If the conference is convened in the future, the commercial treaty and navigation rights must also be proposed. Judging by their intentions, it seems that they still do not want to deal directly with our central government, do not recognize and accept our Ministry of Foreign Affairs' declaration, and want to use the difficult issues of proposing commercial treaties and navigation rights as a plan to delay the conference. As for Mo Dehui's statement to people that if the Sino-Soviet conference can be convened, in addition to discussing the Chinese Eastern Railway issue in accordance with the central government's declaration, navigation rights and commercial treaties will not be mentioned, in order to comply with the central government's diplomatic intentions.

Second Court Hearing of the Gao Ying Appeal Case 83

The Result is Further Investigation of Evidence from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs

The appeal case of Gao Ying and his wife was heard once by the Jiangsu High Court last winter. Because it was still necessary to transfer the case to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for investigation of evidence from San Francisco, the procedure was more time-consuming, and Gao and Liao requested an extension due to childbirth, resulting in a delay of many days. Only today (the 1st) was the second court hearing held. At 1 PM, people from all walks of life arrived in droves to observe, totaling more than 290 people, with women accounting for about 40%. At 2 PM, the Presiding Judge Huang Bingdao, Judges Zhao Zhengzhang and Zheng Zhiguo, Prosecutor Sun Xiyan, and Clerk Qin Qijun entered the courtroom and took their seats. At the same time, Gao Ying, Gao Liao, and Sun Yuan were brought to the court. Gao Ying's lawyers, Liu Shifang and Wang Youling, and Sun Yuan's lawyer, Hu Zhen, also appeared in court. After Judge Huang asked the three people their names and ages, he ordered Sun Yuan and Gao Liao to retire to the side seats. Prosecutor Sun Xiyan stood up and stated that the reasons for the appeal had been explained during the last court hearing and would not be repeated. At this point, Judge Huang began the interrogation.

First, interrogate Gao Ying: Judge (Q): When you were the consul in San Francisco, did Gao Liao bring eleven pieces of luggage when she returned to China from the United States after her first trip? Gao (A): There were fourteen pieces in total. (Q): Did all fourteen pieces of luggage have seals? (A): No seals. (Q): An investigation has been conducted with the Chinese consulate in San Francisco, and photos have been sent back. The luggage clearly has seals on it. You can take a look. (The judge handed Gao the photos for review, totaling three. The first showed eleven pieces of luggage with seals, the second showed three pieces of luggage without seals, and the third showed one of the eleven pieces of luggage with seals. These photos were taken in San Francisco.) (Q): Are these seals from the consulate? (A): No. (Q): Then where did these seals come from? (A): They were probably from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (Q): Were they issued to the consulate by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs? (A): No. (Q): Even if the seals are from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, does your consulate have seals? (A): The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has seals, but the consulate does not have seals. (Q): Does the embassy have seals? (A): It also does not have seals. (Q): According to you, do our Chinese embassies in the United States not have seals? Do their luggage not need seals when they come and go? (A): They do not need seals. (Q): Of the fourteen pieces of luggage that Gao Liao brought, were three pieces her own, and the other eleven pieces were brought on behalf of others? (A): Yes. (Q): According to the photos sent by the San Francisco consulate, all fourteen pieces of luggage have seals. (At this time, the judge showed Gao Ying the photos again, saying that there were seals on eleven pieces of luggage in the photos.) (A): These are not seals. Even if they are seals, I did not know about them in the United States beforehand. I cannot forge seals. (Q): You just said that the luggage did not have seals, but the photos clearly show seals. Since you say there are no seals, where did these seals come from? (A): The luggage was sent from China. I was not in China. Perhaps these seals were affixed in China. As for where they came from, I do not know. (Q): Do the several people named Shen Guang and others exist? (A): Yes, they exist, but I do not know them. (Q): They sent letters to your consulate. How can you not know them? (A): I certainly

do not know them. Now I have evidence to present in rebuttal. The judge ordered him not to present it and ordered him to step down.

Next, interrogate Gao Liao: Judge (Q): You did not accept the judgment of the Jiangning District Court, so you came here to appeal. Are the reasons for the appeal the same as before? (A): Yes. (Q): Did you have eleven pieces of luggage when you went from China to San Francisco? (A): There were fourteen pieces in total, three were my own, and eleven were brought on behalf of others. (Q): Were the eleven pieces entrusted to you by Chen Sheng? (A): Yes. (Q): Did all fourteen pieces of luggage not have seals on them? (A): No, my own three pieces did not have seals. (Q): Did the other eleven pieces have seals? (A): I did not see them at first. I only saw them on the ship later. (Q): How could you not see the things that people entrusted to you? And when the luggage is loaded onto the ship, you need to fill out a customs declaration form, and you must inspect the items. How could you not see them? (A): I did not see them at that time. (Q): When you declared customs, were all fourteen pieces filled out together? (A): They handled it, not me. That's why I didn't see the seals. (Q): Now the San Francisco consulate has already sent photos. The luggage you brought at that time clearly had seals. (He immediately showed her the photos for review.) After Gao Liao reviewed them, (A): My luggage is not in these photos. (Q): Is your luggage not among these fourteen pieces? Then is all that is shown in these photos not your luggage? (A): These eleven pieces were all entrusted to me to bring. (Q): Where is your own luggage? (A): My own three pieces were taken away at that time. (Q): It is true that these eleven pieces have seals, right? (A): Yes. (Q): Where did these seals come from? (A): I don't know. (Q): Would you not know about the luggage you brought yourself? (A): They wrote to me and asked me to bring it, so I don't know. (Q): Gao Ying said that these seals came from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Do you know about it? (A): I don't know. (Q): Are you four

Page 10

going to the United States in April? (A): No, I went in June. (Q): Did you not go to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to get seals when you went? (A): No. (Q): Does the consulate have seals? (A): No. (Q): Are there seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in the consulate? (A): Also no. (Q): Where do the several people named Shen Guang live in Hong Kong? (A): I don't know. (Q): What about Chen Sheng? (A): I don't know either. (Q): Last time you said he lived on North Sichuan Road in Shanghai, but you didn't know where on North Sichuan Road he lived. Now we have already asked the Shanghai Provisional Court to investigate. Because North Sichuan Road is very long, they couldn't find him either. Do you know the street number where he lived? (A): I don't know.

Next, interrogate Sun Yuan: Judge (Q): Have you been at the San Francisco Consulate for many years? (A): Yes, seventeen years. (Q): Did the consulate originally have seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs? (A): No. (Q): Did the consulate have its own seals? (A): Also no. (Q): Are there any in the embassy? (A): I'm afraid not, I haven't seen them. (Q): Are the seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs from before 1927, or are they from the National Government after 1927? (A): There are also no seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government in the consulate. (Q): Since there are no seals, the San Francisco consulate has sent photos, and the luggage at that time had seals on it. Take a look. After Sun Yuan reviewed them, (A): These are not seals. (Q): Then what are they? (A): I'm not sure. (Q): You see, these are also not seals from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs? (A): I don't know. (Q): Since there are no seals in the consulate, it can be seen that they were obtained from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (A): I don't know. (Q): Do the four people named Shen Guang live in Hong Kong? (A): I don't know. (Q): They clearly have letters to you. If you don't know them, why do they have letters to you? (A): I certainly don't know them. (Q): According to their letters to you, the four people named Shen Guang said that they have dealings with the Guangdong Bank in Hong Kong. We have now investigated the Guangdong Bank in Hong Kong, and they replied that there are no account holders with these names. At this point, the judge had the documents from the Guangdong Bank in Hong Kong, transferred by the Guangzhou Court, given to Sun Yuan for review. (To be continued)

Minutes of the International Opium Convention 84

Chinese Representative's Speech Expressing Hope for Cooperation in Eradicating Narcotics

Geneva News: The current session of the International Opium Committee was held from January 20 to February 14, 1930, at the secretariat of the League of Nations International Federation in Geneva. Official representatives from the governments of twelve countries, including China, Germany, France, Great Britain, India, Italy, Japan, the Netherlands, Portugal, Yugoslavia, Siam, and Switzerland, attended the meeting. The United States government sent non-official representatives to observe. The Executive Yuan assigned three specialized assistants, Mr. Henri Brenier, Mr. L. A. Lyal, and Mr. H. E. Snks. The representatives from various countries were all familiar faces from previous sessions, except for the Japanese representative Mr. Sato, who was replaced by Mr. Ito due to the London Naval Conference. In addition to the representatives and specialized assistants from various countries, when discussing the issue of private trafficking in opium and narcotics, the committee invited Mr. T. W. Russel Pasha, the police chief of Cairo, to attend the discussion on the situation in Hungary. A representative from the Hungarian government also attended. At the first meeting, Mr. W. E. van Wettum from the Netherlands was elected as the chairman, and Mr. Gastan Pourgois from France was elected as the vice-chairman. The chairman expressed his welcome to the newly appointed Chinese representative, Mr. Wu Kaisheng. The following is a record of Mr. Wu's speech at the meeting:

Chairman, the report submitted by the Chinese government to the Advisory Committee on the Traffic in Opium this year contains a summary of 1928. This is one of the important tasks in opium control. At the first to third meetings, our country's representatives had already expressed the determination of the Chinese National Government to strictly prohibit opium and other narcotics. Today, I can tell you that this determination has been put into practice. Please read this year's report. It can be seen that the new opium prohibition regulations promulgated on September 10, 1928, clearly express the Chinese intention to prohibit opium in these regulations, so there is no need for me to elaborate. You all have many years of experience and deeply understand the difficulty of prohibiting opium and other narcotics. The Chinese government, in view of this difficulty, in addition to revising the existing laws, is also engaged in great reforms in the administrative field to respect the teachings of the late Generalissimo, who said: "To achieve the goal of opium prohibition, the National Government must adopt a nationally consistent plan." In the past, only because of the influence of the domestic political situation, the government was unable to make active reforms. As political stability was achieved, the National Government studied the situation at that time and specially organized a National Government Opium Prohibition Committee in 1928, which exercised the highest authority to handle opium prohibition matters. The members of the committee are selected by the National Government and the Military Affairs Commission, such as military commanders from various regions, relevant ministers in charge of opium prohibition affairs, and representatives from the National Anti-Drug Association. According to Article 2 of the National Government Opium Prohibition Committee Charter, its main functions are to receive orders from the National Government, supervise and be responsible for strictly prohibiting opium throughout the country, and to investigate opium prohibition and report to the government, which are also the responsibilities of the committee. In addition to handling administrative affairs, the National Government Opium Prohibition Committee also pays close attention to education and cooperates with anti-drug associations organized by the people in various regions, as suggested by the League of Nations General Assembly. The China Anti-Drug Association has now expanded its organization and spread throughout the country, and its development is truly amazing. The National Government Opium Prohibition Committee has not been established for long, and its ultimate success can also be predicted. As for the problem of prohibiting opium smoking, although there were many obstacles in the past, we can happily announce that we have gradually achieved satisfactory results. It should be known that the evil habit of opium smoking will be gradually eliminated due to the joint efforts of the government and the people. However, it is regrettable that illegal smuggling and the use of opium to manufacture narcotics have increased compared to before. Most of China's toxic drugs are smuggled in from various countries. Whether the National Government's opium prohibition efforts can succeed depends entirely on whether the smuggling of these toxic drugs can be stopped. I am not shifting responsibility to others, but I must announce to all countries that they should cooperate sincerely with each other. The Chinese government has long expressed its goodwill and determination. Today, the people of the whole country continue to work hard to find ways to prohibit toxic drugs. I say this in the hope that all countries will cooperate in a spirit of cooperation and work together to promote it.

Local Correspondence

Jiading 85

Robbery of a Coffin Occurs in Nanxiang: At the Zha Creek funeral home in Nanxiang, the coffin of a deceased woman surnamed Zhou was stolen and broken open on the previous occasion (the 30th). The corpse's burial clothes and jewelry were completely stripped away. It was discovered by someone yesterday morning. The family reported it, and the case was forwarded to the Public Security Bureau, which is strictly investigating it. It is rumored that the stolen jewelry is worth as much as eight or nine hundred yuan.

Public Decision on Formaldehyde Alcohol Verification: Seven or eight out of ten wine merchants in this county mix formaldehyde alcohol. At the end of last month, the County Public Security Bureau discovered twenty urns of formaldehyde alcohol and five hundred urns of tax-evading old wine at the newly opened Zhou Zhenxin winery in Ximen. In addition to handing over the tax-evading old wine to the Public Sales Bureau for punishment according to law, all the formaldehyde alcohol was stored in the county government. Now, County Magistrate Chen has summoned various public institutions to decide on a solution at the county government at 10:00 a.m. today (the 1st). It was decided that a small bottle would be drawn from each urn in public and sent to experts for verification. If it is indeed formaldehyde alcohol, it will be severely dealt with according to law.

Kunshan 86

Ransom Date Set for Kidnapped Victims in Zhangpu: Fifty-seven people were kidnapped by lake bandits in Zhangpu Town. Although eleven people were released a few days ago, more than forty people have not yet been released. It is now known that Chen Qiaosheng, who was released from the bandit den yesterday, said that a compromise had been reached regarding the kidnapped individuals. The total price is thirty-eight thousand three hundred yuan, and it has been agreed that the money will be prepared and taken to a certain place for redemption on the fourth day of the lunar month. Currently, Chen is notifying the families of the kidnapped to gather the money and go to redeem them.

Lake Bandits of Yangcheng Lake Have Fled: At 6:00 a.m. on the 31st, the entire battalion of the First Battalion of the 28th Regiment of the Fifth Division stationed in Kunshan, as well as the No. 20 patrol boat of the Provincial Water Police Twelfth Team, and the Kunshan County Police Team Public Security Bureau Chief Wang Zhengben, led by Battalion Commander Kuang, departed from Bacheng and launched a suppression campaign against a large group of lake bandits in Yangcheng Lake. At 10:00 a.m., they arrived at the bandit den Yang Santai Temple, but the bandits had already fled upon hearing the news. It is said that they went towards the Zhengyi area, entered the Shahu Lake, and entered the Huangtiandang, fleeing into Taihu Lake. The military police then burned down the temple and patrolled around for a week. At 4:00 p.m., the entire team returned to Bacheng. Today, the soldiers of the First Battalion departed to return to Kunshan. The County Police Team is still stationed there.

Resignation of Party Consolidation Committee Approved: Wang Yifang, the Consolidation Committee Member and Minister of Organization of the Kunshan County Party Affairs Consolidation Committee, repeatedly requested to resign from the Provincial Party Headquarters due to illness. His resignation has been approved. The vacancy will be temporarily filled by Xu Yongji.

Fengxian 87

Handling of Household Registration Donation: The household registration donation in this county, originally called the "house number fee," was resolved by the second local council last year to levy one jiao to cover the costs of clearing the countryside. Later, due to insufficient budget, it was proposed to add two jiao in the first administrative meeting. Later, because the "Regulations for Clearing the Countryside" had not been promulgated, it was not implemented. In terms of defense, the county police team was勉qiang(reluctantly) allocated according to districts, but it was only one squad per district, which was often felt to be weak. Since the robbery in Ruan Lane occurred, rumors have become more prevalent. Therefore, the county government meeting changed the original proposal to "household registration donation" to be used to establish a temporary police team. It was then submitted to the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments for instructions that the county should establish a temporary police team. The method was concise, and the required funds had already been discussed to be collected through household registration donations, which was also acceptable. It was also submitted to the Provincial Government Meeting for approval and compliance. However, after the garrison troops were transferred to other places last month, the defense became even more vulnerable, and the local people were frightened and requested the opening of the project. Therefore, the county government ordered the first district chief to draft collection methods and immediately established a detachment to increase its strength. It is now known that the case has been instructed by the Civil Affairs and Finance Departments, stating, "The case was submitted by the Provincial Government No. 1288, and this Department submitted that the county should collect household registration donations for four months, one jiao per household per month, as temporary police team funds. It was ordered that the case be submitted to the Government Committee for the 1170th meeting, and it was decided to approve it. You should immediately inform the county magistrate to comply with this order, etc." Upon receiving this, it was found that the case had been submitted by the county before, and it had been forwarded and instructed as the situation warranted. Now, due to the previous reasons, it is necessary to instruct the county magistrate to comply with this order. Therefore, County Magistrate Hong has publicly recorded the order today and issued a notice for compliance.

Additional Notes on Robberies in the Four Townships: The trend of robbery in this county has been slightly reduced since the police team successively cracked down on a large number of bandit dens. However, multiple robbery cases have occurred again this month, such as the Zhang surname in the 48th Tu and the robbery case on the Shaji Road of Fahua Bridge. Last night, the home of Lu Caigen in Baiyun Temple was also robbed of clothing and more than two hundred yuan in cash. In addition to sending personnel to investigate, the county has ordered the water and land police teams to arrest the suspects together.

Songjiang 88

Disputes After Divorce Judgment: Chen Yunyu, a student at an adult women's school, married Yang, who lived outside Dongmen, nearly six years ago. The couple had a good relationship. However, her husband worked at a pawnshop in Shanghai, and his elderly mother had a mental illness. Family affairs were usually managed by his unmarried eldest daughter. The sisters-in-law did not get along. Last year, due to a tenant issue, Yunyu was forced to leave home and began studying at the school. Her family then sent a letter to her brother to return home, accusing Yunyu of "disobeying her mother-in-law" and "secretly fleeing with belongings." Her husband, without investigating, directly filed for divorce with the county government. After interrogation, it was found that the accusations were unsubstantiated, and the plaintiff lost the case. However, after the judgment, the couple lived together for several days. Ms. Yunyu even found her own belongings, such as children's hats, in her husband's sister's room, proving that they had been hidden and then falsely accused of being stolen. Her husband still returned to work in Shanghai, and another incident occurred at home. The matter was heard by the clan, who all disapproved of what the Yang family had done. Fearing an incident, they invited Ms. Yunyu to temporarily live at her aunt's house, waiting for her husband to return to Songjiang for mediation. Unexpectedly, the Yang family recently filed an appeal and secretly burned Ms. Yunyu's clothing and bedding. Ms. Chen has reported this to the Fourth District Police Station, which has dispatched police to investigate. She is also seeking justice everywhere. Those who hear about it sigh for her.

Account Books Seized from Opium Den: The county government received a report yesterday that large-scale sales of opium lamps were occurring in the Third District of this city. Police Chief Dong Futang, along with many police officers, secretly went to search the premises. They found Xu Wanggang's opium den and two opium smokers, Yang Xiaomei. They also seized two account books, which fully recorded all business transactions and offerings. The trial officer, Du, sentenced the den owner, Xu Wanggang, to six months in prison, fined the opium smoker, Yang Xiaomei, forty yuan, and confiscated the account books and other evidence.

Wuxi 89

Major Fraud Case Involving Impersonating an Official Sentenced: Jiang Jingxian from Shanghai, previously impersonated a relative of an official and defrauded Yang Gubai from Liyang of one thousand yuan, claiming to help him get the position of Public Security Bureau Chief of Nanhui County. Later, because the promotion failed, Yang took him to the Public Security Bureau, which transferred him to the county government for interrogation and detention. It is now known that yesterday afternoon, the County Government Trial Officer Yu sentenced Jiang in court. In the private prosecution, he was also ordered to repay Yang Gubai one thousand yuan. After hearing the sentence, Jiang declared in court that he was not satisfied and requested that the judgment be delivered quickly so that he could appeal.

Jiangyin 91

Armed Troops of the Police Team Demand Pay, Which Has Been Issued: The county police team had not been paid for two months. On the 30th of last month, all the armed troops rioted. The troops only calmed after County Magistrate Shen explained and persuaded. Yesterday (the 31st), Director Shen sought a way to arrange from various villages, with the guarantee of Chen Jingshan, the director of finance, using the county surtax as collateral. He borrowed 3,400 yuan from Fengtaiyuan and 3,300 yuan each from Baochang and Yongcheng, totaling 10,000 yuan, to pay off the two months of back pay. The remaining funds will be issued separately. The expenses of other institutions are based on the police team's salaries, with a monthly budget of 1,745.50 yuan.

Trial Date Set for the Sihe Tragedy: In the case of Xue Shibao's brutal killing of Huang Wangchun and others in Tangtou, Sihe Township, after the county government's initial court hearing, Xue Picheng and Liu Deming, the injured parties, had recovered from their injuries and submitted their medical reports to the county. The case is under investigation. Due to the transition of trial officers, the hearing and judgment have not continued. Xue Shibao's side stated that the shooting and killing of Huang Wangchun and Chen Ruilin were accidental deaths and injuries and was willing to declare bankruptcy to provide compensation. He requested his relatives, Xi Lusheng and others, to mortgage all his fields to provide compensation. The families of the deceased Huang Wangchun were to receive 20 mu of rented land and 1,000 yuan for funeral expenses, the family of Chen Ruilin 10 mu of rented land and 500 yuan for funeral expenses, Liu Deming 250 yuan for medical expenses, and Xue Picheng 500 yuan for medical expenses. Yesterday (the 31st), he submitted this to the county, requesting approval so that the funds could be distributed separately. Xue Picheng's side also stated that since the tragedy, both sides regretted it and did not want to be enemies. Therefore, they also submitted a statement to the county stating that Xue Shibao's criminal behavior should be dealt with by the authorities according to the law. County Magistrate Shen has set the court date for April 7 and ordered the police officer Jin Chuyun to summon Xue's wife, Xue Peixiu, Xue Peiying (Xue Shibao's daughters), Xue Yufeng, Xue Zhensheng, Xue Wangshi, Huang Youbo, Xue Rongbao, and others for questioning.

Yangzhou 92

Jin Yunpeng Tours West Yuhu Lake: Jin Yunpeng, a counselor of the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs, came to Yangzhou from the capital yesterday and toured the scenic spots of West Yuhu Lake. He stayed at the home of his close friend. On the 30th, he went from Yangzhou to the capital and then to Henan, reportedly with an important mission.

Continued Interrogation of the Robbery of the Fujian Steamer: Regarding the robbery of the Zhengtong Company's Fujian steamer and the tugboat Fengxian Guangji at Baotawan, the Sixth District of the Postal Police, stationed in鎮江, sent personnel to Yangzhou on the 30th to thoroughly investigate the scene. It was revealed that two bandits boarded the steamer as passengers in鎮江. When they reached the bay, they pretended to call for disembarkation and ordered the steamer to stop. When a flashlight flashed, several bandits jumped aboard and went directly to the official cabin, robbing Principal Xiao of Suqian Middle School of more than 200 yuan. The passengers in the official cabins and other cabins suffered some losses. Fortunately, the tobacco shed passenger cabin was not affected.

Township Heads and Deputies of the Sixth District Petition: Tian Zaishan, the township head and deputy of the Sixth District, and more than 40 others, representing the entire district, organized a petition group. They arrived in Yangzhou at 8:00 a.m. on the 30th and visited the county magistrate to petition. In addition to submitting a petition listing the seven major crimes of the district chief, they also recounted all his misdeeds. The county magistrate agreed to investigate and deal with the matter according to the law. Next, they went to the Party Headquarters, where they were received by Standing Committee Member Tang Shou, who also agreed to forward the petition to the county for unanimous assistance.

Jingjiang 93

Bandits Kill in Ji City: At 7:00 p.m. on the 27th, four bandits suddenly arrived at the home of a shoemaker across from the pawnshop in Jishi City. Without asking any questions, they dragged the shoemaker out and beat him to death before leaving.

County Government Purchases a Large Number of Firearms: The county government previously collected 17,500 yuan to purchase firearms from the Department of Civil Affairs because of the bandit police in neighboring counties. The firearms arrived yesterday, totaling 110 rifles, each with 500 rounds of ammunition, priced at 145 yuan each. They have now been successively distributed to the local defense corps in each district for use.

Nantong 94

Post-Suppression Conference: The army, navy, police, and joint forces suppressed bandits in the eastern townships. Now, the bandit remnants have retreated to the Caopengzhen area and are stubbornly resisting the government forces. On the 31st, representatives from the Party, government, military, police, and industry held a post-suppression conference at the county government and resolved the following: (1) Send representatives to petition the central and provincial authorities and the military and political authorities in the Shanghai-Songhu area to allow the army, navy, and police in Nantong to be exempt from transfer until all the bandits in Nantong are eliminated. (2) The representatives will jointly form a慰問队 (weiwentui; comfort/consolation team) to work in the eastern townships. (3) The county police brigade lost 77 rifles and a large number of bullets during the suppression. The brigade commander, Yan Diannan, is responsible for recovering them within the shortest possible time. The county government will request the provincial authorities to punish the negligent captains Xu Guanxiong and Wu Xuzhai. The police officers who had their weapons seized by the bandits will be dismissed, and the existing troops will be thoroughly reorganized.

Local Bandits of Juegang Have Been Repelled: A large group of bandits was discovered in the Baitu Temple area of Juegang. More than 20 police officers were killed or injured. The provincial police team and the Taiyuan迫擊砲队 (poji paodui; mortar team), which happened to be passing through the area, provided assistance. The bandits suffered many casualties, and a large number of weapons and ammunition were seized. The mortar team arrived in Tongcheng on the 31st and proceeded to Yu Dong.

Captured Bandits Escorted to the City: The provincial police team suppressed bandits in Eryuan, Qian'an District. On the 31st, they repelled a group of bandits, killing one bandit and capturing four. The captured bandits were escorted to the city for interrogation.

County Court Requests Direct Reporting of Criminal Cases: The county court believes that criminal cases involving people from various townships and towns are reported to the county government or the Public Security Bureau, which takes time and makes investigation and verification difficult. It has requested the county government to order all districts to report directly in the future to simplify procedures and expedite the process.

Rugao 95

Bandit Leader Wang Pengnian Arrested: Wang Pengnian, a bandit leader wanted by Rugao with a reward, was captured by the Niuzichao unit of the Third Squadron of the County Police in the Shizhuang Six Jia area. Wang uses the alias Guo Zifang and claims to be a pig seller. The police captain Niuzichao escorted him to the County Clearing and Suppression Bureau for legal proceedings. The bureau interrogated him, but he firmly denied using an alias. Therefore, the bandit was transferred to the county government for interrogation.

Further News of Bandit Disaster in Luzhuang: The wife of Lu Zifang of Luzhuang fled north of the village during the bandit riot a few days ago. Unexpectedly, she encountered five bandits halfway, who grabbed her, held a knife to her neck, and thoroughly searched her, robbing her of several hundred yuan in cash. Fortunately, she was not injured. It was also said that Lu Jiade, a local gentleman in the village, was in dire straits. During the bandit riot a few days ago, he was dragged out of his house by the bandits, who beheaded him with a kitchen knife, killing him instantly. Lu Bangxun fled to Lujiagang during the bandit riot and encountered a large number of bandits, who shot him several times, killing him and robbing him of six or seven hundred yuan in cash hidden on his body.

Shen Jinghua Handles the Handover: Shen Jinghua, the former director of the County Public Security Bureau and the current director of the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau, came to Rugao yesterday (the 27th) with County Magistrate Zhang. It is said that Shen's trip was specifically to handle the handover of his duties during his tenure. He will stay for a few days to complete the official business and then return to Shanghai.

New County Magistrate Takes Office: The new County Magistrate Zhang Yi arrived in Rugao by car from Tongcheng in the morning and went to the county government to take over. He will be sworn in on a selected date.

Execution by Firing Squad of a Robbery and Murder Offender: Gu Mingchuan from Haimen County, a tenant of the Huafeng Company, committed robbery at the home of Gu Desheng in Juegang last year and shot and killed Gu Demao, Gu Dequan, and five others. He was captured by the Clearing and Suppression Branch Bureau. His confession was confirmed. He was sentenced to death by the county government and approved by the provincial government. He was escorted to the execution ground on the afternoon of the 26th and executed by firing squad.

Huzhou 96

Bride and Guests Kidnapped by Bandits: Fang Jinkui, who lived in Changtan Village, about four miles from Daixi Town in the southern part of this city, was quite wealthy, and bandits had long coveted his wealth. On the 28th, when Fang Jinkui was taking a second wife, guests filled the house to congratulate him. Unexpectedly, at around 5:00 p.m., more than ten bandits suddenly arrived, each holding wooden shell guns, and swarmed in. The guests fled in panic, allowing the bandits to rob all the clothing and decorations. Before leaving, they abducted the bride and three guests, Chen and Gao. The family immediately reported to the security team and the Public Security Bureau, which dispatched team members to pursue them, but the bandits were nowhere to be found.

Jiaxing 97

Crackdown on Profiteering Merchants Hoarding Food: The retail price of rice in Jiaxing has risen to 16 yuan per shi (a unit of dry measure), while traders are asking for 16.50 or 16.60 yuan. Rice merchants are requesting the評議會 (pingyi hui; council) to allow price increases due to capital losses. The council has decided that the current price is temporarily limited to 16 yuan and will not be increased. It will then submit a request to the county government, which will forward it to the Department of Civil Affairs, requesting that the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs allow Zhe省 (abbreviation of Zhejiang Province) merchants to purchase several tens of thousands of shi of rice and instruct rice merchants to purchase as much 洋米 (yangmi; foreign rice) as possible in Shanghai to provide relief. On the other hand, the county government has formulated five measures to crack down on profiteering merchants hoarding food and issued them to rice merchants for compliance: (1) Local merchants and wholesalers who hoard food with the intention of profiteering and obstructing the people's food supply will be dealt with according to these measures. (2) Local merchants and wholesalers should report the amount of grain stored each month to the county chamber of commerce, which will forward it to the county government for verification. If there is a case of underreporting, the remaining grain may be confiscated. (3) The grain stored by merchants should be sold to anyone who wants to purchase it at the market price and should not be refused. (4) If the grain stored by wholesalers is not sold for a long time, they should provide reasons and report them to the county chamber of commerce, which will forward them to the county government for verification. If the county government considers the reasons insufficient or deems it necessary to regulate local food supplies, it may order them to sell it at the market price. (5) Those who hoard food and refuse to allow purchases or refuse to comply with the county government's order to sell it may be punished or have their goods confiscated, depending on the severity of the circumstances.

Hangzhou 98

West Lake Museum Scheduled to Open: After the closing of the West Lake Exposition, the Zhejiang Provincial Government decided to establish the West Lake Museum in the buildings of the Zhonglie Temple and Wenlan Pavilion in order to promote cultural research and science. Chen Junhuai was appointed as the curator. After taking office, Curator Chen actively prepared, repairing the buildings and collecting items. However, there are not many exhibits in the history and culture department, while the natural science department has a full range of exhibits, including various groups of animals, plants, minerals, and other exhibits. Because of the beautiful spring weather and the opening of the National Games, people from all over the country are flocking here. Therefore, the museum is scheduled to open on April 1 for people to visit.

Ningbo 99

Chairman Chiang Leaves Ningbo for Hangzhou: National Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and his wife, Soong Mei-ling, returned to their hometown of Fenghua on the 22nd to sweep the tombs. They suddenly decided to return to the capital after ten days, but it did not materialize. Yesterday (the morning of the 29th), they finally set off. Chairman Chiang received a telegram from Zhang Jingjiang, the chairman of Zhejiang Province, inviting him to attend the National Games and inspect the Fifth Army Instructor Group. Therefore, he decided to go to Hangzhou and then to the capital. Yesterday morning at around 8:00 a.m., he and Soong Mei-ling, Soong Tzu-an, Lin Sen, Zhang Zhizhong, Chen Shaokuan, and others traveled from Xikou, Fenghua, to Ningbo by car. When the car reached the South Suburb Bus Station in Yin County, the cylinder suddenly exploded, and the car could not move. Therefore, Chiang and Soong switched to covered sedan chairs to the Jiangbei Cargo Station. Security was very strict along the way. It was already 10:10 a.m. He immediately took a special car to Hangzhou. Military, police, and political officials of Ningbo City all came to the station to see him off. Naval Commander Chen Shaokuan sent Chiang to the car and then went to the Chu Zou warship, leading the Jiankang warship to leave Ningbo and head to Shanghai to await orders. Zhang Zhizhong and others still took the car with Chairman Chiang to Hangzhou. At 11:53 a.m., the car arrived at Wufu. Chairman Chiang changed into military uniform, got out of the car to inspect the instructor group, and gave a speech to the new recruits. At 2:15 p.m., the car arrived at Cao'e. After crossing the river, he switched to a car and went straight to the riverside in Hangzhou.

Shaoxing 100

Chairman Chiang Passes Through Shaoxing to Hangzhou: Chairman Chiang of the National Government, accompanied by Madam Soong and others, arrived at Wufu from Ningbo at 8:00 a.m. on March 30 to inspect the garrison. In the afternoon, he crossed the E River and took nine cars and twenty or thirty guards to Shaoxing and then to Hangzhou at 3:00 p.m. The county magistrate and representatives of various institutions and organizations welcomed him at the Wuyun Station. Because Chairman Chiang needed to go to Hangzhou urgently, he did not stop in Shaoxing. The adjutant got out of the car to greet the representatives. On that day, the provincial government also sent troops to Shaoxing for security.

Shen Bao Education News National Games Special Issue (Second Issue)

Grand Opening of the Games Yesterday 101

More than 10,000 Athletes Arrived from Twenty-Two Provinces and Cities

Chairman Chiang Gave Two Addresses Encouraging the Masses

Unprecedented Grand Occasion on the West Lake A Scene of Extraordinary Excitement

Tianjin, Liaoning, Beijing, and Shanghai All Achieved Good Results

Grand Opening 102

After months of preparation and widespread publicity, the unprecedented National Games opened at the Hangzhou Meidong Gaoqiao Stadium at 9:00 a.m. yesterday. National Government Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, Madam Soong Mei-ling, Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, Finance Minister Soong Tzu-wen, Naval Vice Minister Chen Shaokuan, Central Committee Members Shao Lizi, Wu Zhihui, Chu Minyi, Chen Guofu, Zhejiang Provincial Government Chairman Zhang Jingjiang, Games Chairman Dai Jitao, Preparatory Director Zhu Jiahua, Deputy Director Zhou Xiangxian, and others personally attended. Twenty-two provincial and municipal delegations and more than 2,000 male and female athletes participated. The number of spectators was so large that there was no space available. Those standing surrounded the stadium in several circles, totaling no less than 10,000 people. This was truly an unprecedented event in the history of sports in our country. The order was maintained by male and female Boy Scouts, and everything was in good order. The music was uplifting, and the cheers of the crowd created a magnificent and fresh atmosphere. After the athletes from each province and city arrived, they paraded around the stadium. Amid the applause, the flag-raising ceremony was held. The details of the opening ceremony are recorded below.

Spectators Filled the Seats 103

Before the opening of the Games, representatives from the central government and important officials from the Zhejiang Provincial Government arrived in succession. The rostrum had several levels, covered with red felt. For a time, the seats were filled with dignitaries. In the center of the opposite field, prizes were displayed, surrounded by levels, like silver towers shining in the sunlight. At around 9:00 a.m., Honorary Chairman Chiang and Madam Soong arrived. Chiang was led into the stadium by an attendant, carrying his overcoat, looking around with a calm demeanor. Photographers rushed to take pictures. After Chiang took the stage, he greeted everyone and took a seat. The sound of military music filled the air. The spectators' seats were so crowded that there was almost no room to stand. At 9:00 a.m., the entire group of athletes, led by the military band, entered the stadium, following the predetermined order. Each team was led by a flag, followed by instructors and staff, then female athletes, and then male athletes. Every time a province or city passed in front of the rostrum, applause erupted. Chairman Chiang stood and watched from afar, applauding with even more vigor. The entire group circled the stadium twice and then stood in designated areas. Then, a cannon was fired to open the Games.

Participating Organizations 104

Yesterday, the following organizations were in attendance as spectators: the Physical Education Survey Team of the National Chengdu Normal University, the Police Academy, the Sergeant School, Huai'an Middle School, Huaiyin Middle School, Zhongshan Institute of Physical Education, the Boy Scouts, Pudong Middle School, Shanghai Middle School Boy Scouts, the High School Attached Elementary School, Hongdao Girls' Middle School, Pumin Girls' Middle School and its elementary school, Provincial First Middle School, the School for Orphans of National Revolutionary Army Soldiers, the Chinese Women's Physical Education College, Jingzhi Elementary School, Yumin Elementary School, the junior high school section of the junior high and senior high schools of the Chongwen Elementary School, Yongjin Elementary School, the Board of Directors of Pudong Middle School, the 10th, 16th, 6th, and 5th elementary schools of the urban area, Ningbo Middle School, Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School, the Boy Scouts, Huian Girls' School, the Women's Vocational Advancement Elementary School, the Municipal Senior High School and its affiliated elementary school, Jingzhi Elementary School, Chengxi Elementary School, and the Hekou District Elementary School, among dozens of other organizations.

Attendance 105

At the opening ceremony, there were 19 representatives from various provinces and cities, 66 advisors to the congress, 197 members of the congress, over 6,000 participating guests, over 1,850 athletes from various provinces and cities, over 400 referees and staff members of the congress, over 1,700 primary school students from Hangzhou, over 400 military and police personnel, over 300 reporters from various provinces, and over 100 photographers.

Opening Ceremony Protocol 106

1. Firing cannons (playing music)

2. All staff and athletes parade around the field

3. Take seats

4. All remove hats and stand in solemn silence

6. Sing the Party song (playing music)

7. Bow three times to the national flag, the Party flag, and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen

8. Chairman Chiang respectfully reads the will of Sun Yat-sen

9. Three minutes of silence

10. Chairman Dai Jitao delivers the opening address

11. Shi Weihuan delivers the address on behalf of Vice Chairman Zhang Jingjiang

13. Director Zhu Jiahua reports on the preparations

15. Chairman Chiang delivers a speech

17. Athletes' oath ceremony

18. Chairman Chiang delivers a speech to the general representatives of various groups

19. Speeches by Mr. Wu Zhihui, Mr. Wang Zhengting, and Mr. Chu Minyi

20. Shout slogans

21. Photography

22. Group performance (Hangzhou primary schools)

Before entering the field, the athletes gathered in the square of the organizing committee. Led by military music, they entered through the main gate. The order of the procession was: Hangzhou primary school students, Hubei, Guangdong, Hong Kong, Anhui, Jiangxi, [unclear character], Liaoning, Fujian, Hunan, Dongte [Special Eastern Provinces], Ping [Beiping], Tianjin, Kobe, Jing [Nanjing], Jiangsu, Shanghai, Sichuan, Abei [Northern Argentina], Zhejiang.
