Two Important Telegrams from the National Federation of Commerce 181

Urging a Delay in Lace Inspection—To the Honorable Executive Yuan, Ministry of Industry, Commerce, and Finance of the National Government in Nanjing: We have received a telegram from the Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipality Lace Embroidery Trade Association, stating, "Our companies and firms have received a public letter from the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce on March 12th, stating that lace is a handicraft product of our country and also a part of foreign trade, with about 500,000 women across the country depending on it for a living. In addition to the original telegram on file, which is not redundantly described, we request the Federation of Commerce and all chambers of commerce to unanimously support and present our difficulties, requesting the abolition [of the inspection]." Attached are detailed rules signed and noted to the meeting. In response, we believe that the first essential for commodity inspection is standards. Lace embroidery has thousands of variations in patterns and designs, with different products and different times. To establish a standard for inspection would be difficult and obstructive. The reason is the same as why it is impossible to establish an exchange for silk fabrics, as there are too many patterns that change frequently. As for the excessive fees and the dispatch of personnel for guidance, those are secondary issues. This industry belongs to handicraft products and is a major part of our country's recent foreign trade of domestic goods. In recent years, merchants' capital has been insufficient, and they have suffered from foreign economic encroachment. Domestic merchants are merely entrusted to use their money. In the past, the Ministry of Finance, considering domestic goods, specially exempted various types of transit taxes, as documented in two orders. To maintain and develop this industry, we should find ways to help increase its capital to facilitate business and prevent profits from going to foreigners. If inspection is carried out without standards, it would not be in line with the policy of encouraging handicraft products for foreign trade and protecting women's handicrafts. The association feels this is a crisis and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we are sending this telegram to your esteemed Yuan and Ministries for review, requesting that the inspection of lace be temporarily delayed until the trade association is formally established. At that time, they should be ordered to establish regulations and improve product quality to facilitate foreign trade. In this way, promotion and support would still have the intention of advancement, and both commercial and industrial sectors would benefit greatly. We are deeply grateful." Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce; Su Minsheng, Zhang Yuquan, Lu Guangji, Chen Riping, Li Kuian, Peng Chuli, and others, kowtow.

Requesting the Maintenance of Swatow Telephone—To the Honorable Executive Yuan, Ministry of Transportation, and Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government in Nanjing; and to the Honorable Guangdong Provincial Government Construction Department in Guangzhou: We have received a report from Chen Zhiying, executive committee member of the affiliated association, representing the Swatow General Chamber of Commerce, stating that the Swatow-Chaozhou-揭陽-普寧 long-distance telephone company, run by merchants, was established in the ninth year of the Republic and approved by the provincial government. In the seventeenth year of the Republic, the Construction Department approved the registration and issued a license. In February of this year, part of the shareholders' stock was transferred to Ren Shou Tang and Jin Cheng Tang, who were original shareholders. On March 9th, a letter was received from the Swatow Electric Bureau, stating that, according to the Ministry of Transportation's order, the merchant-run telephone company must submit an application for registration to the Ministry within one month. While complying with this order, on the 20th, a letter was suddenly received from the Swatow Electric Bureau, stating that, according to two telegrams from Yuan Hao of the Ministry of Transportation, the company was illegally established and that the private transfer of business to Ren Shou Tang was even more inappropriate. It should be taken over by the Ministry, and the original capital of 12,000 yuan would be repaid from the surplus, etc. The Electric Bureau then forcibly took over the company. The company petitioned the Swatow General Chamber of Commerce for support, and the Swatow General Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Transportation requesting the withdrawal of the Ministry's takeover order. A letter was then sent to the factory committee, reporting to the association requesting assistance. In addition, Lu Shaofan, the company's representative, reported to the association, stating the same as above. The company was founded ten years ago, and the provincial government and departments approved the registration, so it was not illegally established. The capital was not just 12,000 yuan. As for the transfer of stock, it is a common practice for merchant-run companies. Ren Shou Tang, namely Chen Pengqiu, the former vice president of the Swatow General Chamber of Commerce, is indeed a legitimate businessman. At a time when the regulations protecting privately-run electrical enterprises have been promulgated, if a privately-run telephone company is suddenly nationalized, it would be contrary to the original intention of maintaining privately-run companies. Moreover, according to the report from Representative Lu, the case occurred because Chen Xinyu, a partner who had quit the company, falsely accused the Swatow Electric Bureau, which then telegraphed the Ministry. Therefore, the other three merchant-run telephone companies in Swatow have no problems. Considering this, it seems that there is suspicion of favoritism. An investigation should be sent to clarify the truth. In order to respect the law and maintain commerce, the association is jointly telegraphing your esteemed Yuan and Ministries for review, requesting a prompt withdrawal of the Ministry's takeover order and a return of the company to merchant management for reorganization and compliance with the deadline for submission to the Ministry for registration. We also request the provincial government and departments to instruct the Swatow Municipal Government to protect the company. We hope for a telegram in response. With deep gratitude, Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, et al.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Maintains Yangtze River Traffic 182

Upstream Steamers Have Stopped—The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company originally had ten ships operating on the Yangtze River. As of yesterday, the Shanghai branch of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has canceled the upstream routes from Shanghai to Hankow, and there are temporarily no ships operating today. Furthermore, the Sanbei Company's Chang'an and Dexing ships cannot sail downstream, so there are no ships available to Hankow, resulting in a suspension of service. There will be no Chinese ships sailing on the Yangtze River from Shanghai this week.

Fourteen Ships to Suspend Service First—The Shanghai Navigation Industry Association, in order to maintain traffic and commerce on the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, has invited representatives from various shipping companies to a meeting to discuss ways to balance commerce and transportation. It is reported that yesterday's discussions resulted in the designation of six ships from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which had temporarily suspended services, and the agreement to suspend service for eight ships from Sanbei, Zhaoxing, and other companies, for a total of fourteen ships. If further suspensions are necessary, they will be discussed again today and shared among the companies.

Three Major Yangtze River Ships Can Return—The Jianghua, Jiangshun, Jiangxin, and other ships of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company that are currently in operation are the top-tier ships among the Chinese-owned Yangtze River steamers, referred to by the company as the "Three Major Yangtze River Ships." Their operations have ceased this time upon arrival in Hankow. Because this concerns the lifeline of the business, Li Yunliang, the business section chief who is in Hankow for inspection, has repeatedly negotiated. Yesterday at noon, a telegram was received from Li, stating that the Three Major Yangtze River Ships can all depart from Hankow and sail eastward to Shanghai in approximately four or five days. Starting next week, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company may be able to operate one or two ships on the Yangtze River.

The Water Conservancy Commission Dredges Sandbars—The Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission of the Ministry of Transportation has specially dispatched Acting Engineer Li Qianruo to Shanghai to inquire with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company about the shallow shoals and sandbars in the Yangtze River in preparation for dredging. The company has submitted its opinions, stating that the Shanghai-Hankow waterway is constantly changing, with the riverbanks on both sides also collapsing and silting up. The problem with the river flow is that it has not been guided to follow the natural course, resulting in the blockage of many important waterways. During periods of low water, navigation is extremely dangerous. For example, in the Yadan Zhou waterway upstream of Huangshigang, the hidden sandbar and narrow waterway in Lanxi on the upper reaches, the customs house specifically prohibits night navigation during low water and sets up red flag, black ball, and light vessels to warn of the dangers. In recent years, merchants have suffered greatly. Taking advantage of this low water period, dredging should be carried out as soon as possible. The Water Conservancy Commission will base its actions on this proposal and conduct a preliminary survey.

More Ships Are Stopping Upstream—Since the labor strikes by boatmen in Chongqing and stevedores in Yichang, an increasing number of foreign-owned ships are suspending service to Shanghai. There are currently four British ships and three Japanese ships that cannot sail upstream and are therefore staying in Shanghai, anchored idly in the Huangpu River.

Yan Ruling Escapes Danger – Other Reports 185

Well, well, well, Bullets flying everywhere

Twisting stairs evade danger

The bandit den is luxuriously decorated

The hotel has a secret setup

Yesterday, this newspaper gave a detailed account of Yan Ruling's escape from kidnapping. Further reports have been received describing the circumstances of the arrest, and they are recorded here. Jin Jiulin, Special Agent Detective Inspector of the French Concession Police, after investigating and confirming that the bandit den was located on the third floor of the Western-style house at 356 Jin Shenfu Road, reported to West Inspector Sachair. Together with West Detective Inspector Belgie, West Detective Gélanti, Chinese Detectives Li Yaolong, Mao Jingen, Qian Yumin, and Bao Detectives Zhou Yaoting, Zhang Ziying, Zhou Buguang, Qin Youyu, and more than ten others, they fully armed themselves and drove to the location in cars on the evening before last to make the arrest. Upon reaching their destination, the detectives scattered to ambush and surround the bandit den. Chinese and Western detectives knocked on the back door, and a bandit answered. The detectives immediately captured him. The bandit shouted loudly, "Well, well, well." Upon hearing this, the bandit guarding the hostage on the third floor knew that the detectives had come to make arrests. He took out a pistol and a Mauser pistol at the staircase and opened fire downwards to resist arrest. The detectives also opened fire in response. Nearly eighty shots were fired. Fortunately, the staircase in the Western-style house was circular and winding, allowing the detectives to dodge and rush upstairs fearlessly. They captured two bandits in the pavilion room on the second floor. Seeing that the situation was not good, the kidnappers on the third floor opened the windows and fled to the roof. The detectives also chased onto the roof and captured four or five people. At the same time, they rescued the hostage. In total, more than ten kidnappers were captured, including Zhang Fengxiang, Zhou Bingcheng, Tao Jinbao, Wang, A Da, Fang Youshan, Luo Shisheng, and others. They were handcuffed together in a chain. Then, three pistols, one Mauser pistol, and nearly twenty bullets were found in the bandit den. After the search was completed, the hostage and the bandits were taken to the police station in separate cars. First, the hostage was escorted home. Then, the detectives interrogated the bandits and learned that secret setups were located in the Dongya and Central Hotels. Detective Jin led the detectives to the British Concession Police Station and, together with Chinese and Western detectives, went to the two hotels. The bandits had already fled upon hearing the news. The detectives reported back to the West Inspector, who ordered a strict search for the bandit gang to bring them to justice. It is reported that the bandit den was luxuriously decorated, with the rooms full of mahogany furniture and equipped with telephones.

Coincidentally, Another Madwoman is Discovered 186

Topless, Wielding a Knife and Axe

Again Staging a Violent Scene of Chopping People with a Knife

A Second Landlady Chopped Five Times

The Injuries are Severe and Life-Threatening

Wang Quanfu, a local from the Fan Family Residence at 19 Hongzhen, earns a living as a laborer. He rents out his spare rooms to Wang Da, a Tongzhou rickshaw puller, and his wife, Cao, who is 47 years old. Last year, she suffered from a mental illness, but was later cured. Her husband Da did not know that it had recently relapsed. At around 9:00 AM yesterday, Wang Da went out to pull a rickshaw, and Cao's old illness relapsed. She was topless, holding a knife in her left hand and an axe in her right. She barged into the room of Wang Shen, the wife of the second landlord Wang Quanfu. At the time, Shen was just getting out of bed. Seeing Cao wielding a knife and an axe and stumbling in, she was greatly alarmed. Cao did not say a word and went straight to the bedside, drew the blade, raised the axe, and chopped at Shen. Shen was, after all, a woman, and could only shout for help. Her head and face were chopped in more than five places, and she fainted to the ground while bleeding profusely. The madwoman Cao then began to wave her hand. At that time, a patrol police officer from the Hongzhen Police Station of the Fifth District, Third Precinct Public Security Bureau happened to be passing by Dexingli and heard cries for help. Following the sound, he saw the truth and arrested the madwoman. When asked why she killed someone, she spoke incoherently, only saying, "I couldn't stand it, it's nothing." The victim, Wang Shen, is 34 years old. After the incident, she was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Because the injuries are severe, her life is in danger. This incident and the murder case by a madman that occurred in the Nanshi district a few days ago are truly coincidental.

The Madman's Life Can Be Saved 187

But His Foot Must Be Sawed Off

The events of the madman, Zhang Jiazhen, killing one woman and one child and injuring another child in front of the Qunxue Society on Zhonghua Road have been recorded in previous newspapers. After the Yang Prosecutor of the local court accepted the case, he ordered the bailiffs to go to Xinpuyu Hall to examine the madman and ask him the reason. Unexpectedly, he still answered with the words "Heaven ordered me to kill them." After the bailiffs reported back, Prosecutor Yang, together with Secretary Mao and Inspector Shen, went to the court yesterday morning to conduct an inspection. The madman's injuries can be guaranteed not to threaten his life, but his foot must be sawed off; otherwise, it will spread to other parts, and the danger is unimaginable. When asked why he killed, he still gave no coherent answer. The official then instructed the hall to report if the madman could be cured so that the case could be investigated.

Robbery and Kidnapping with Injuries in Xinchang Town, Pudong 188

A Mother Takes a Bullet to Save Her Son

At around 9:00 PM on the night before last (the 31st), more than ten robbers suddenly came to the home of Ni Ruicheng, a villager behind Ni Jia Temple, about six li north of Xinchang Town in Pudong. Showing pistols and Mauser pistols, they threatened and intimidated, and arbitrarily searched for valuables. However, the family of peasants had no valuable possessions, only a few cloth clothes. They kidnapped his son, Yongsheng, and took him away. At this time, Ni's wife, Ma, was deeply attached to her son and could not bear to part with him. Disregarding the danger, she stepped forward to stop them. The robbers turned around and fired several shots, one bullet hitting her left leg. Bleeding profusely, she fainted to the ground. The robbers then left. The injured woman hired a boat to Shanghai at dawn and was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Water Pipes Connected on Shiqing Road, Zhabei 192

The Section of North Sichuan Road Has Been Installed

The Zhabei Water and Electricity Company is adding an 8-inch diameter pipe to Shiqing Road to connect the existing two small-diameter pipes, which are insufficient to meet the increased water demand from the newly built houses on both sides of the road. The new pipe will connect to the pipes on Yokohama Road in the south and Xingjiazhai Road in the north to form a circulating water flow and to provide relief in case of a failure in the Dongbaoxing main pipe. However, the section crossing North Sichuan Road is a road built by the Public Concession outside its boundaries. The company submitted a request to the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities to negotiate with the Public Concession Council for the issuance of a road excavation permit. The Bureau then sent a letter through the Municipal Government Secretariat and obtained the agreement of the Council. The company has now completed the installation in the section of North Sichuan Road and will continue to bury the pipes on Shiqing Road.

The Public Concession Sees a Decrease in Vehicle Accidents in the First Three Months 193

The Shanghai Times reports that the number of fatal vehicle accidents on the roads of the Public Concession in the first three months of this year has decreased compared to the same period last year as a result of public cooperation with the police. As of yesterday, only twenty-seven people have died in vehicle accidents this year, compared to thirty-three in the same period last year. Of these twenty-seven deaths, ten occurred in March, eight of whom were due to their own carelessness, and two of whom were due to the drivers' fault. The police have charged those responsible with manslaughter in the Provisional Court. In addition, 320 people have been injured this year. Bicycles are the most difficult vehicles for traffic police to manage. There have been a total of 105 bicycle accidents in the past three months, injuring twelve people. There have been 725 car accidents, killing eight people and injuring 254 people. There have been 487 accidents involving various types of hand-pulled vehicles. Among the bicycle accidents, 43 were due to the fault of the riders. This is because these vehicles are often ridden by minors who often disregard all safety regulations, leading to frequent accidents. Therefore, some have proposed increasing the registration fee to regulate them. The roads most prone to accidents are still Nanjing Road, Xizang Road, Jing'an Temple Road, and North Sichuan Road.

Their office is located at 18 Zhenpingli, Grolot Road. They were sworn in yesterday. Representatives from various agencies and the French Concession Federation of Commerce attended to offer congratulations. Director Yuan Inspects Pudong Yesterday 195

Director Yuan of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, accompanied by Section Chiefs Song Yuntao and others from the Second and Third Sections, took a small patrol boat to Pudong at 9:00 AM yesterday to inspect the Third District Office, the First Sub-office, and the Fourth Police Squadron and its affiliated agencies. Xu, the captain of the water patrol team, also accompanied them to Pudong. After arriving at the First Sub-office of the Third District in Yangjiadu, they conducted a detailed inspection and then walked south to the Laobaidu Police Station. Director Yuan paid close attention to the diligence of the officers on duty along the way. After inspecting the police station, they took the original boat north at the ferry and docked near the Lan Nidu Wharf. Detectives Zhang Yong and Yang Jinsheng from the Third District greeted them ashore and escorted them directly to the Third District Headquarters. By this time, it was noon, and they had lunch in the district. District Chief Zhang Wuqin then summoned all the patrol officers and chiefs from the district and the various foreign factories to the district headquarters. Director Yuan inspected them and then gave a speech. He said that the police are public servants and should act with integrity. The only goal of the police is to eliminate violence, maintain order, and prevent harm. Therefore, they should do their best to maintain peace and stability. Local officials should especially lead by example and avoid any improper acts such as corruption or embezzlement. The director of the bureau uses personnel impartially. All officials are personally examined and hired. Recommendations from private individuals are not accepted. Rewards and punishments are clearly defined. For example, seven patrol chiefs have recently been promoted to patrol officers for their good service to encourage them. Therefore, the police should strive to improve themselves step by step. The director also has an ideal to train the city's police force to become a model for the entire country to achieve the goal of recovering the concessions in the future. It is hoped that everyone will work diligently and faithfully, and that the officials unite to benefit the region. The director has high hopes for this. After the speech, they inspected the district's dispatch room, household registration office, detention center, and the district chief's office, expressing satisfaction. It was not until 4:00 PM that they walked to the Fourth Police Squadron in Lujiazui for detailed inspection and then took the original boat back to the bureau. It is reported that tomorrow they will continue to go to Pudong to inspect the Second Sub-office of the Third District in Yangjingzhen and the Fourth Sub-office of the Third District in Gaoqiao.

A Frightening Large Market Robbery 196

Su Xiaodi, a 44-year-old resident of the Su family pond house in Tangqiao, about eight miles north of Dachang Town in Baoshan, was in financial straits, so he entrusted a middleman to sell his six mu of farmland. At 10:00 a.m. the day before yesterday, he received a deposit of 50 yuan. Unexpectedly, at about 10:30 p.m. the previous night, more than twenty bandits, wearing blue cloth shirts and trousers, speaking with a local accent, and with their faces painted in various colors, went to Su's house, kicked open the door, and rushed in. They pulled out handguns and threatened Su Xiaodi to hand over the full price of the land. Su dared not resist and immediately took out the 50 yuan deposit and handed it to one of the leading bandits. The bandits suspected that Su was intentionally withholding the full amount, so they beat Su all over with iron bars and ordered him to reveal where the money was hidden. In great pain, Su randomly claimed that the land price was hidden in a stone cave at the foot of the Tangqiao Bridge. The bandits believed him and forced Su to lead them to the bridge abutment. Su tried to jump into the river to commit suicide, but was pulled back by the bandits and taken back to Su's house. They took the large iron pot used for cooking rice from the stove, then overturned Su naked onto the stove and burned firewood under the stove. Su's chest and abdomen were burned by the fire, and he cried out for help. The bandits clapped and laughed wildly, then fled eastward, firing several shots before leaving. Although nearby farmers heard the noise, they dared not help. After the bandits left, people went to Su's house to check, but Su Xiaodi had been burned so severely that his condition was critical. In addition, Xu, the 32-year-old wife of Cao Fusheng, a resident of Caobing Lane, about four miles southeast of Dachang, ran a burlap bag shop in Zhabei in this city. She returned home to sweep the tombs the day before yesterday morning. At about 11:30 p.m. the previous night, she was also robbed by similar face-painted bandits. The bandits robbed Cao Xu of a pair of gold bracelets, two rings, clothes, and more than 20 silver yuan. After succeeding, they also stripped her naked, placed her on the stove, burned firewood, and fled with shouts. After people went to rescue her, her breasts and lower body were burned. The scene was too horrible to look at. Afterwards, both the Su and Cao families reported to the Dachang Township branch of the Baoshan County Public Security Bureau and the Dachang Security Corps. However, the police force was weak, and the head of the Security Corps, Lu Fengpu, was accused by the members of failing to take responsibility, allowing the bandits to escape. Yesterday, the Public Security Bureau had already sent detectives to arrest them everywhere.

The Liujing Bridge, south of Jinjiazhai in the Caobing District of this city, is a stone-slab bridge. The bridge piers were damaged by boats and supported by wood. Now the supporting wood is rotten, and the bridge is tilted, threatening to collapse. The Municipal Public Works Bureau considers the bridge to be a transportation hub in the vicinity and occupies an important position. To facilitate pedestrians, it has specifically requested the Municipal Government to allocate 1,000 yuan to rebuild the wooden bridge.

Fierce City Tigers Make Travel Difficult 202

An Old Woman Injured, Two People Dead

An Old Woman Staggering Along: The Shanghai-Minhang-Nanzhe long-distance bus, the 1:00 p.m. bus driven by the newly hired Pan Liansheng, who had only been working for three days, caused an accident on the Shenkai-Minhang route. As the bus was approaching the south end of Zhuanqiao Station on the main road, an old woman, about fifty years old, suddenly staggered across the road. Pan Liansheng repeatedly honked the horn, but she ignored it and continued to walk, so the bus was unable to give way and knocked her down. The front of the bus grazed the left corner of the old woman's forehead, causing her to bleed profusely and lose consciousness. She was later revived after being rescued. The impact also slightly damaged the engine of the bus, rendering it unable to run. The company was notified and sent personnel to repair it. The passengers were carried by another bus. At the same time, the injured old woman was sent to Minhang Hospital for treatment.

A Hawker Careless: Zhang Apei, a 60-year-old local hawker living in Xiaonanmen, was struck by a private car No. 6226 driven by Jiang Zidong, residing at No. 99 Xiafei Lane, Xiafei Road in the French Concession, as he was walking through the area on the afternoon of the 12th of last month. Zhang was knocked down and injured his head, and died on the ground on Pushi Road the next day. The police reported to the police station, and the body was taken to the autopsy center. Judge Zhu of the French Court came to the center to verify the cause of death. Finding no relatives of the deceased, the court arranged for burial. Yesterday, the police summoned Jiang to the French Court for questioning. The head of the Vehicle Department first testified, explaining the previous situation. Questioned, Jiang Zidong testified that the deceased was walking from north to south and bumped into the rear wheel of the merchant's car. When the merchant realized it, he immediately stopped the car, but the deceased had already fallen to the ground. The police arrived and helped him into the car. At that time, the deceased was conscious. He took him to the hospital for treatment. According to the doctor, the injury was not serious. After applying medicine, he was discharged from the hospital. He accompanied him to the police station. After questioning, the police chief determined that the deceased was not careful and ordered the merchant to give him two yuan to go home and rest. Later, he did not know how, the deceased fell to the ground and died at Pushi Road. He found that the merchant's car was driving very slowly at the time, and it was indeed the deceased's own carelessness that caused the accident. He asked for investigation. Then, patrolman No. 446 testified that he was on the scene that day and saw that the defendant's car was driving very slowly. The Chinese and Western officials ruled that it was indeed the deceased's carelessness, and the case should be closed.

A Woman Requests Dissolution of Marriage 203

Chen, a resident of No. 318 Yuqing Lane, Zhaofeng Road, and engaged in the automobile business in Pudong, whose given name is Guiying and is 19 years old, was betrothed to Qu Miaofu of No. 4 Zhongshi Lane, Yangjiadu, Pudong, when she was ten years old, with Chen Achun as the matchmaker. They were scheduled to marry this spring. However, Chen Guiying claimed that the marriage was not agreed to by her and hired lawyer Ye Kang to file a petition with the District Court requesting dissolution of the marriage, stating that the defendant's side had contacted her father and hastily arranged the marriage. The defendant, Qu Miaofu, has no permanent employment, is idle all day, and is habitually dissolute. As this concerns her lifelong happiness, she requested permission to dissolve the marriage. Yesterday, Judge Yang Keqian held a hearing in court. The defendant did not appear. According to the plaintiff Chen Guiying's testimony, she is 19 years old and a local. (Question) When were you engaged? (Answer) In the tenth year of the Republic [1921], when I was only ten years old. It was entirely decided by my parents. My mother is now deceased. (Question) How much betrothal gift was there at the time? (Answer) Gold bracelets, gold rings, and gold ruyi hairpins, etc. (Question) Who was the matchmaker? (Answer) The matchmaker was Chen Achun, who is now deceased. (Question) Why do you want to request the dissolution of the marriage? (Answer) He has no job. (Question) Did you know this when you were engaged? (Answer) I knew it, but I was very young at the time. (Question) Why didn't you come to the last hearing? (Answer) Because the defendant's side asked someone to negotiate and settle it out of court, and asked me to request to withdraw the case, so I didn't go last time. Unexpectedly, they went back on their word and ignored it. (Question) Can it still be reconciled out of court? (Answer) There is no possibility of reconciliation. The judge then invited prosecutor Liu Pingfan to the court to express his opinion. The plaintiff's lawyer then rose and stated that the National Government adopted a lenient policy toward the dissolution of marriage. If one party disagrees, the marriage can be dissolved. Therefore, the dissolution of marriage is different from divorce, so the court must carefully consider and judge divorce cases. The plaintiff in this case was only ten years old when she was engaged and had no judgment. Now she hears that the defendant's side is planning to marry her soon, so the plaintiff suddenly panicked. Although the plaintiff's age has not reached the age of autonomy in marriage, considering that the defendant has no profession and the future is bleak, for the sake of her lifelong happiness, she has no choice but to request permission to dissolve the marriage. The judge then announced the end of the debate and adjourned the hearing to await the verdict.

New System for Manchuria Railway Freight 208

Implementation of the Metric System

Every year, a large amount of goods are transported from Shanghai to the northeastern provinces, such as Fengtian, Changchun, Andong, Niuzhuang, and Gongzhuling. The South Manchuria Railway accounts for most of the goods transported. The Dalian Steamship Company, affiliated with the railway, is the joint transportation agency for passengers and freight. Due to the success of its business in recent years, it has plans for a major expansion this year. The company's freight transport has always used Japanese shaku and kan, as well as British and American pounds and yards. It is now announcing to the Dalian Steamship Company in this city that it is changing to the new metric system. It is said that 64 countries in the world use this new system, so the company is also changing its regulations. Currently, in China, only the Jichang Railway uses the metric system for freight. For example, if a carload of goods is calculated at 33 American tons, which is 49,816 catties, it becomes 30 tons if the metric system is used. In fact, 104 catties can be loaded more. In the new system, "length" includes (1) micron, abbreviated as (mu), which is one millionth of a meter; (2) millimeter, abbreviated as (hao), which is one thousandth of a meter; (3) centimeter, abbreviated as (li), which is one hundredth of a meter; (4) decimeter, abbreviated as (fen), which is one tenth of a meter. Also, one meter is equal to 3.3000 Japanese shaku, 3.2804 British feet, or 1.09361 yards. One "ton" is equal to 0.62137 miles, one "metric ton" is equal to 0.98420 British tons and 1.1023 American tons. The new freight rates for the metric system that have been set are specially recorded as follows:

(Destination) (First Class Freight Rate) (Second Class Freight Rate) (Third Class Freight Rate) (Fourth Class Freight Rate)

Dan/Ton Yuan Dan/Ton Yuan Dan/Ton Yuan Dan/Ton Yuan

Fengtian 1.85 12.53 1.50 10.28 1.15 7.51 0.80 5.32

Tieling 2.15 14.81 1.73 12.14 1.32 8.85 0.92 6.29

Kaiyuan 2.28 16.12 1.83 13.10 1.40 9.60 0.97 6.37

Andong 3.20 N/A 2.59 17.60 1.96 12.88 1.35 9.00

Niuzhuang 1.59 N/A 1.29 8.34 0.99 6.32 0.70 4.35

Changchun 3.42 23.52 2.72 18.83 2.08 14.20 1.40 9.62

Gongzhuling 3.15 21.41 1.52 17.17 1.93 12.98 1.32 8.73

The above freight rates are calculated in Japanese yen. Shanghai must also pay in Chinese currency according to the market price. This metric system is new to Shanghai, so it is specially recorded in detail.

Relief for Bovine Plague Near Shanghai 212

Commodity Inspection Bureau Succeeds in Manufacturing Bovine Plague Serum

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce believes that the prevalence of bovine plague in our country causes losses of no less than tens of millions of yuan every year. Even the milk farms in Shanghai and its vicinity suffer significant losses every year due to bovine plague and the death of cattle. The bureau's veterinarians Yi Wenzhi, Luo Qingsheng, and technician Shou Biao believe that this is a problem for China's animal husbandry industry and must be urgently addressed. In addition to their inspection work, they have been researching the manufacture of bovine plague serum. The bureau strongly supports their proposal and has rented five mu of land on Tiyu Road, Jiangwan, and purchased many cattle for experiments. It is now reported that the experiments have been successful, and the manufactured serum has been tested repeatedly and proven to be sufficient to resist bovine plague. It is said that five cattle were used in the first experiment and four cattle in the second experiment. The experimental methods were divided into two types: (1) Inject the manufactured serum into the healthy and disease-free cattle, and then inject blood poison (i.e., blood containing bovine plague bacteria) into the cattle at the same time. The cattle do not show any symptoms and are permanently immune to bovine plague. (2) Inject blood poison into the healthy and disease-free cattle, and the cattle develop disease. Then inject the manufactured serum into the cattle, and the cattle recover. The results were very satisfactory. The bureau now plans to further demonstrate the greatness of its effectiveness from multiple perspectives and in practice. It plans to send letters to the Shanghai Special Municipal Municipal Committee Offices and the Shanghai County Township Government, stating that the bureau can provide injections free of charge when bovine plague occurs in the townships to ensure that the experiments are more accurate. It is said that Wu Tingyang, the former director of the Guangxi Construction Department, and Niu Houze, the Gansu disaster relief representative, greatly admired this plan and the success of the experiment, and personally visited Jiangwan to observe the cattle. Niu Jun said that Gansu province has more than 4 million cattle, and many cattle die from bovine plague every year. He expressed enthusiastic sympathy for the manufacture of bovine plague serum and said that he would like to study manufacturing there in the future.

However, the association's relief funds have already been fully allocated. It is now necessary to raise funds urgently to avoid delaying the relief period. A resolution was proposed on how to raise funds. Resolution: Actively raise funds and simultaneously telegraph the provincial government to request additional allocation. The meeting adjourned.

Jisheng Association Pleads for Disaster Victims 215

Letter to the National Government

The Chinese Jisheng Association writes that disasters have spread everywhere, and the people cannot bear their suffering. First, due to the lack of water conservancy, droughts and floods persist. Second, due to the presence of soldiers and bandits everywhere, the people are fleeing. Third, due to the failure of agriculture, production has decreased, leading to a shortage of rice in the south and wheat in the north, with reliance on imports from foreign countries. If the leak is not stopped, the foundation will be depleted. If we only focus on emergency relief, we must encourage increased agricultural production and remove obstacles to agriculture, industry, and commerce. Otherwise, empty talk of saving the country will lead to unimaginable consequences. With compassion, we appeal to the national government ministries and relief associations, pleading and beseeching them on behalf of the people. We have no choice but to raise our voices. The original manuscript is provided below. Wang Zhen, Chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Jisheng Association, and Vice-Chairmen Xu Mao and Huang Qinglan, wrote to the National Government Executive Yuan, Ministry of Interior, and Relief Commission: Our association is currently handling relief in dozens of counties in the seven provinces of Shaanxi, Suiyuan, Pingyuan, Anhui, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu. The amount of relief funds spent is significant. However, based on reports of disasters from various provinces and counties, the area we are providing relief to is only one or two thousandths of the total area affected. It is a drop in the bucket, and universal relief is difficult. The dire circumstances reported are all based on the personal experiences and observations of our association's relief directors and staff, who have conducted on-site investigations. They are not based on hearsay or vague impressions. In the disaster areas, some people have died from cold and starvation due to the heavy snow and extreme cold last winter. Others have committed suicide due to years of drought and floods, facing famine. They are cooking bones, eating flesh, selling their wives and children, losing their homes and families, and separating from their loved ones. Corpses are everywhere, leading to the spread of epidemics. It is a human hell, an unprecedented disaster. The situation is especially dire in the Northwest. Nearly half of Shaanxi's population has died, and misfortune is spreading. In Suiyuan, fields are barren, and there is no ability to sow seeds, leading to a hopeless autumn harvest. There is no one to appeal to. Even in the relatively prosperous regions of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, the disaster in more than ten counties north of the Yangtze River in Jiangsu and more than ten counties in Wenzhou and Taizhou in Zhejiang is severe. The hardship and displacement are beyond description and are unprecedented. The reasons for this are that first, due to the lack of water conservancy, any natural disaster, such as drought or flood, becomes unmanageable. Second, due to the presence of soldiers and bandits everywhere, those with some savings are relocating to better places. Third, due to the failure of agriculture, production has decreased, leading to soaring grain prices and public panic. Trade relies heavily on other countries, and economic control is in the hands of foreign merchants. Money flows out, and prices double. If this leak is not stopped, the foundation will be depleted. This is not just a matter of survival for people in disaster areas but will become unsustainable in the long run. Furthermore, with consecutive years of famine and poor harvests, not only will the famine victims in the Northwest fill the ditches, but the people of Jiangsu and Zhejiang will also face a similar fate. Our association considers disaster relief our duty and does not meddle in other affairs. We are deeply concerned about helping the needy and alleviating suffering. We have always done our best to provide disaster relief in provinces such as Shandong, Henan, Anhui, and Shaanxi. We also carry out work relief to promote agriculture, prevent floods, and alleviate droughts. Now, during the period between the exhaustion of last year's harvest and the availability of the new crops, poor farmers have no means of livelihood, and there are many who cannot afford seeds. If we do not provide assistance now, planting will be delayed, and there will be no harvest in the autumn. If we face another famine year, the remaining people will face extinction. In the past, disasters only affected a few provinces or dozens of counties. Now, there is almost no province or area that is free from disaster. A great catastrophe has befallen us, which was unexpected. The situation requires urgent action. Our association is acting on our conscience to provide long-term planning for disaster victims. Our strength is insufficient, and we must appeal for help. Your esteemed office is the central authority for the whole country, and the welfare of the people is your concern. You should provide relief to the starving and open the granaries. How should we ensure that planting is not delayed, that production is increased, that the people can live in peace, and that farmers can work in peace? We hope you will review, consider, and implement measures to encourage and inspire them. Our association, on behalf of hundreds of millions of disaster victims, is deeply grateful and awaits your command.

Investigation of Stamp Tax Implementation Methods in Various Countries 216

The Shanghai Manufactured National Goods Factory Association believes that stamp duties on documents provide legal protection and are recognized as legitimate taxes in various countries. However, the implementation methods vary. Therefore, the association requested its permanent lawyer, Mr. Wang Zhengshao, to consult and investigate the matter at various consulates. The following is a report based on Mr. Wang's findings: (1) United States: According to investigations at the US Commercial Counselor's Office and the US Consulate General in Shanghai, invoices for cash transactions are not subject to stamp duty. However, for other non-cash transaction documents with a term of more than twenty days, a stamp duty of one cent is levied per 100 yuan (refer to the 1924 US Stamp Tax Regulations). (2) United Kingdom: According to investigations at the British Consulate General, invoices for the sale of goods, other than payment receipts, are not subject to stamp duty. For various securities subject to stamp duty, the value must be at least two gold pounds (approximately equivalent to more than 20 yuan in national currency). (3) Japan: According to investigations at the Japanese Commercial Officer's Office and the Japanese Consulate General, the rules are the same as in the United Kingdom. The value of the securities subject to stamp duty must be at least 10 yuan. Amounts of 10 yuan or less are exempt from stamp duty.

Record of the Laundry Guild Joint Meeting 218

The Shanghai Laundry Guild held a joint meeting of its executive, supervisory, and standing committees yesterday at 8 PM at 255 Weishui Lane, Ningbo Road, Public Concession. More than twenty people attended, including Zhu Rong and Zhang Liyong. The standing committee member Fang Yunlong was elected as the temporary chairman, and Fang Zhenlei served as the secretary. The meeting proceeded as planned. During the opening remarks, the chairman reported that the guild had been established for nine years. Due to the scattered nature of the industry, the guild's offices were established in two locations: (1) on Hanbili Road, Hongkou, as the Shanghai Laundry Guild, and (2) on Beidiluo Road, French Concession, as the Shanghai Laundry Guild Office. This was initially done for the convenience of industry members. However, current budget expenditures and monthly dues collected are insufficient to cover public expenses. Therefore, industry members have been called together to discuss merging the guild's offices into one location to reduce monthly expenses. A new address has already been selected, and preparations are being made to report to the authorities for record-keeping. Zhu Kunyang reported on the previous income and expenditure. Hu Shanlai proposed that the chairman appoint someone else to review and disclose the previous accounts to the public. Wu Rongfang reported that Fang Yunlong had been appointed as the standing committee member because the guild's internal restructuring had been unreliable. Therefore, he was appointed to reorganize everything. Huang Linqing proposed merging the labor union and establishing a joint labor-management committee to avoid labor disputes. The meeting adjourned at 12:00 AM.

Ministry of Industry and Commerce Approves the Registration of Accountants 219

The Shanghai Accountants Association reported that its members often encountered difficulties when applying to the local industrial and commercial administrative authorities for registration when providing services outside Shanghai, as stipulated in Article 6 of the Accountants Ordinance. Therefore, on February 13, the association requested the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to provide an interpretation for relief. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce replied in document Shang Zi No. 9164, stating that according to Article 6 of the Accountants Ordinance, accountants should directly submit their applications to the local industrial and commercial administrative authorities for approval when performing their duties. Regarding the matter of filing with the court, as stipulated in Article 10 of the same ordinance, the local administrative authority where the registration is sought should notify the court. If an accountants association has not been established in the place where the duties are performed, Article 16 of the same ordinance allows the accountant to join the nearest accountants association. Furthermore, with the exception of those who hold certificates issued by the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce and Ministry of Industry and Commerce of Beijing that have not been verified, all other certificates are naturally valid. The association is hereby notified accordingly.

New Zhong Dian Code for Reducing Telegraph Costs 223

The "New Zhong Dian Code Complete Book" was compiled by Zhang Yanxiang, a graduate in engineering from the New Zhong Engineering Co., Ltd. It was approved by the Ministry of Transportation and registered with the Ministry of Interior, and it is used throughout the country. The content is based on the 1928 International Telegraph Regulations and uses English letters to represent numerical telegraph codes, which can save more than one-third of telegraph costs. Each Chinese character is marked with a numerical telegraph code above and the New Zhong Dian code below. It can also be used as a secret code book for telegraphs, making checking convenient. The book has now been published and is widely sold. Those who wish to save on telegraph costs can study this book.

A: Why do you have so many clocks in your room?

B: Because time is the most precious thing in the world. With all these clocks, all the time is mine.

A: Old Bing saved my life. I'll be grateful to him for the rest of my days.

B: How did he save you?

A: He married my fierce and shrewish fiancée.

Little girl: Mom, I don't want to wash my face.

Grandmother: Good child, wash it well. Washing your face makes you fair and clean. I used to wash my face several times a day when I was young.

Little girl: Look at yourself in the mirror. You washed it too much, and that's why you have so many wrinkles on your face.

Woman: I see something to admire in you, so I'm willing to marry you.

Man: Yes, my father's property will all be mine one day.

Rare News from the Eastern Seas 228

— Qiushui

(1) Eighty Earthquakes in Twelve Hours: According to Japanese communications, there have been extremely numerous and intense earthquakes recently near Atami and the Izu Peninsula. In addition to those observed by residents, the seismographs at the observatory have detected over 700 earthquakes in the past three weeks. The most severe was on Monday the 11th of last week. On average, there have been at least eighty earthquakes per day between sunset and nightfall. Japan is known for its frequent earthquakes, but the number of occurrences this time is rare. However, authorities are somewhat fortunate, as frequent small earthquakes may prevent a severe earthquake. The Tokyo reconstruction project has just been completed, and it is hoped that a major earthquake like the one several years ago will not occur again amidst these seismic events. Residents are living in a state of panic. Most of the wealthy residents have moved elsewhere. It is also reported that the hot springs in Atami have suddenly lost their temperature after the earthquakes. Atami is known for its hot springs and is a popular tourist destination in the spring and summer. This is quite unusual. There are also rumors that a large tsunami will strike the area, which is increasing the residents' fear and leading to more migration. Although the authorities are trying to stop it, it is ineffective. If the earthquakes do not stop, the two areas mentioned above may become ruins.

(2) Reiteration of the Prohibition on Using Lead in Cosmetics: Japanese cosmetics are far inferior to those in Europe and America. Some women's cosmetics, such as powder and face powder, still contain lead. It has been reported that the Ministry of Interior has issued a clear order prohibiting the addition of lead to powder. Cosmetics containing lead are not only harmful to the user's skin, but recent surveys by health experts have revealed that most children who develop meningitis are due to their wet nurses or mothers using lead-based powder. Therefore, the Ministry of Interior has had to issue a strict ban to protect people's health. The prohibition of lead in cosmetics in Japan was previously issued in 1900. However, due to strong opposition from the business community, the decision was postponed. Now, thirty years later, the ban has been reiterated.

(3) Losses from the General Election: During the general election in Japan last month, the public sentiment was boiling, and businesses were shut down. We can see this in the newspapers. Their fervent attitude cannot but stir our patriotic hearts. It is said that the financial losses for both the government and the public during the recent Japanese general election were nearly 10 million yuan. Each candidate had to spend an average of over 50,000 yuan. Most of the money flowed into the pockets of printers. Election matters rely heavily on publicity, and publicity relies on printing, in addition to speeches. Therefore, many printing houses made a fortune from this election. Even in a corner of Tokyo, the money flowing into printing houses reached over 1 million yuan. They are lucky indeed.

Interesting Records from the Jiaotong University 34th Anniversary (Part 2) 229

— Cheng Zhizheng

The Kaleidoscope of the West Dormitory: After the ceremony, the new dormitory rooms were opened to the public. Students had taken the initiative to tidy up and decorate their rooms. Some hung colorful screens, others hung calligraphy and paintings, some designed their rooms like homes, and others hinted at transience. Some emphasized elegance, while others were rich in aesthetic ideas. Some offered fruits to the guests, while others provided paper and pens to solicit inscriptions. It was a kaleidoscope of sights. There were probably hundreds of visitors. The female students of the university were the first to arrive and were full of praise for the rooms. The simplicity of Room 118 was particularly attractive to the guests. The fragrance of clothes and hair added to the charm of the new dormitory.

The Women's Dormitory under the Gaze of Ten Thousand Eyes: Although Jiaotong University has had female students for three years, there has been little interaction between the male and female students. Their dormitory is located in a remote northeast corner, which some have called the "Cold Palace." It has never been open for public viewing in the past three years. This time, to celebrate the anniversary, it was opened for public viewing for one day for the first time ever. Upon entering, the instructor, Ms. Wu Peizi, greeted the guests. Upon ascending the stairs, Ms. Wang Hengling served as the hostess and guided the tour of three rooms. The rooms were richly decorated, and the design was unique. Upon asking for further details, it was said that the other rooms were locked. So-called open viewing was only a small part of the whole. The women's dormitory was originally a faculty residence, so the rooms were not uniform in size, and the buildings were old. The construction of a new women's dormitory seems to be a pressing matter.

A Glimpse of the Entertainment: The afternoon was for entertainment, and there were many programs. The two-person play was the most humorous. Later, a Westerner played the hand organ, and a Western woman played the piano. Their music was excellent. Afterwards, there were fire stick dances and other performances. The evening performance was Beijing opera. Mr. Zhang Zhifu's "Black Windkerchief" was the most eye-catching. There were many female guests in attendance, and order was maintained.

Night Scene Approaching Paradise: When the lights came on, the scene at Jiaotong University changed again. Colored lanterns were strung from the main gate around the playground to the new dormitory. From a distance, they looked like stars. The clock tower and flagpole were illuminated by colorful electric lights. The beauty was beyond description. At that time, women with mist-like hair and swaying skirts walked slowly on the paths. Whispers and chirps filled the flower shadows. This scene was almost not of this world. The show ended at midnight, and the grand event was declared closed.

A Record of Lingering Spring at Fragrant Sea 230

— Jing Mengdie

Early in mid-spring. Wind and rain persisted for weeks. The spring colors were marred by dust. How could one not lament the erosion of spring? The plum garden's floral affairs were mostly unappreciated. Yesterday, at the invitation of Zheng Zhongxiu, an old friend and head of the Jiangnan Tobacco and Alcohol Bureau, I also eagerly thought to visit the garden, as if visiting an old friend I had not seen for a long time. I was also accompanied by Zhang Yunsheng. The three of us drove there. Upon arrival and entering, the scenery of Fragrant Sea was only half or a little more of its former glory. The branches in sight were either sparse or dense, like glimpsing only half of Consort Xu's face. Only the traces of snow on the path and the subtle fragrance filled the air, making all the passing guests like Xun Ling. We chatted casually over tea outside the Song Bin Hall. Zhongxiu said that he would soon be transferred to Yangzhou and would be temporarily separated from the lake and mountains of Xidi, fearing that the two-thirds of the bright moon would evoke dreams of ten thousand plum trees. Therefore, he proposed taking a photograph to commemorate the occasion. I readily expressed my agreement, not only to capture the spring scenery but also to console his longing for the clouds and trees in the future. So, we chose a spot on the lawn in front of Tianxin Terrace and took a photograph together. The figures among the flowers were either sitting or standing, with a peculiar rock adorning the side. The solitary peak stood out, adding to the uninhibited charm. Thus, I inscribed four poems:

Cherishing old friendships in this famous garden, comforting hearts at the edge of the world.

Spring is on the branches, birds its artisans.

My slender shadow is like that of the Kun crane.

I have come to the mountains to accompany the plum blossoms.

Just now emerging from the snow-covered sea, leaving traces of mud,

Like a wild goose flying from beyond the sky, leaving an occasional footprint.

Do not lament the late arrival, the flowers half-fallen,

A wisp of lingering fragrance transforms into a soul of verse.

A delicate stone bears witness to three lifetimes,

Pine and bamboo have an old pact with plum blossoms.

Smiling, I point to the vastness of Lake Tai,

Cherishing this parting for you, recording deep affection.

Zheng Zhuang's heroic spirit gladly pauses his carriage,

Zhang Xu, joining the excursion, is equally delighted.

From here to Yangzhou, moonlit nights will bring,

Two-thirds of the spring colors in dreams of Jiangnan.

Discovery of Mongolian Artifacts and Ancient Books 231

— Li Jun

A friend of mine has been doing business in Mongolia for many years. He sent a letter the other day, recounting the discovery of ancient artifacts and books in Mongolia. It was fascinating, so I have excerpted it below.

Last year, the Russian Oriental Exploration Team, led by Gao Siluo, ventured into the Gobi Desert and other parts of Mongolia. It was deep winter, and the weather was bitterly cold. Gao Siluofu temporarily returned to Moscow, while many of his assistants continued their work, searching for ancient ruins and strange objects. Soon, they discovered an ancient tomb. They began to excavate it. Deep within the tomb, they found a white alum stone coffin. Upon opening it, they found floral felt hangings, various silk items, and many gold, silver, pearl, and jade ornaments. The carvings and workmanship were extremely exquisite, seemingly beyond the capabilities of modern artisans. Finally, they unearthed seven hundred volumes of ancient handwritten books.

The handwriting was small and faintly discernible. The books were written in seven different languages, but only the Chinese and Indian scripts could be identified. The remaining ancient books could not be deciphered. The books were lined with silk brocade and meticulously bound. The book chests were engraved with the inscription "Identified in the third year of Emperor Huizong of the Song Dynasty in the second month." Since obtaining these books, the exploration team has treasured them as priceless gems. It is said that they will be taken back to the ancient artifact preservation center in the Russian capital along with the floral felt hangings and ornaments for display.

Red Rug

Random Notes on Mei Lanfang’s American Tour from the Zhuiyu Pavilion 232

— Lai

Mei Lanfang’s acting made me think of Greek drama. There are discussions of Greek drama in ancient books that are often difficult to understand. Now, watching Mei Lanfang’s acting, I suddenly have some understanding.

The acting in Chinese opera is very real, but not in a photographic sense. It’s an artistic reality that makes the audience feel it is even more real than the original.

My favorite opera to watch is "Assassinating the Tiger," which has a historical and literary atmosphere. The suicide scene is particularly well done.

The acting of most American playwrights feels stiff. Mei Lanfang's acting, from the movement of his eyes to the movement of his sleeves, is just right. His postures are lively and completely free of stiffness.

Some people think that facial expressions should be realistic, but they are not. They also have a set of rules and changes. They are definitely not aimed at superficial expressions of violent emotions.

The placement of each character on the stage in Chinese opera is very good. Mei’s standing position changes from time to time (such as moving forward or backward), but it is always in the most appropriate place. Each change gives the audience a fresh perspective, keeping them from getting tired. Mei's eyebrow makeup is excellent. The arrangement of white, black, and red is like the beauty of ancient porcelain. As for his postures of bowing, looking up, sitting, and standing, they are all similar to ancient paintings.

I have no problem with Mei's falsetto singing. I think the difference between Mei's falsetto and a woman's real voice is equivalent to the difference between imitating a woman's posture in opera and a woman's natural movements. It can be said to be purely artistic. Listening to it, there is no unpleasant feeling.

After Yang Jun's criticism, he asked Wan Hua if there were any errors. Wan said, "The criticism is very appropriate, but I dare not accept it." He repeatedly inquired about various rules of Chinese opera. Wan answered them one by one. Hearing this, Jun slapped the table and exclaimed, calling it true drama. The above is what Yang Jun said, which has not yet been reported, so I have described it in detail. The other New York newspapers often have reports, too numerous to mention.

Since the beginning of Wan Hua's performances, ten new plays have been staged within a week. However, their box office sales are not as good as Wan Hua's. The currently sold tickets are being resold for as much as eight dollars. Considering the current situation in New York, this price is not easy to achieve. However, the general opinion is that we could still fill the seats even if we raised the price to eight dollars. Several of the largest theaters have come to negotiate. One theater (i.e., the National Theater) can hold about a thousand seats. An agreement has been reached, and the performances will move there in the third week. Prices may be set differently in the future.

Warmth in My Heart (161) 233

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Ten: Fiery Flames Rise, Laneway Praises Filial Daughter; Red Carpet Laid, Famous Performers Met on the Spot

Ruiyun said, "Alright, stop trying to whet my appetite. If you say it's good, why wouldn't I go?" A-Jin said, "What new opera is it? Does the stage have all sorts of scenery? Is there a curtain in front of the stage that pulls open, revealing all sorts of scenery that looks just like the real thing?" Zuo Shichen said, "That's right. There are all sorts of unconventional new operas these days. They're gradually becoming popular in Shanghai. They have scenery, curtains, gongs and drums, and singing. It's something called 'neither fish nor fowl.' Theirs is a purely new opera. They've been practicing for months. It's not like those sloppy ones. Anyone can jump on stage and do it. They don't practice at all on weekdays. When it comes time to perform, they end up saying things that don't make sense. This is a real new opera!" Hearing this, A-Jin became even more excited and said, "Little Miss, the new opera is much better than the old opera. They don't have gongs, drums, or singing. They just talk, so it's much easier for us to understand. With those old operas, we don't know what they're singing. If they sing for too long, I'm going to fall asleep in the theater! People who understand singing find it interesting. We don't understand singing. We don't know what they're saying. As for those martial arts plays, we only see red-faced and black-faced people fighting, tumbling, and doing handstands. They're fun to watch, but they keep doing the same old tricks. On the other hand, those new operas have a good plot. We can understand every sentence they say clearly. And it's a complete play from beginning to end. It's not just a piece here and a section there. Second Young Master, if you're inviting Little Miss, I want to go too!" Zuo Shichen said, "Of course. You're indispensable. You're Little Miss's military attendant. Of course, I have to invite you." A-Jin didn't know what a military attendant was. She also said, "When the time comes, we have to be prepared early. But even if Big Aunt lets Ruiyun go to the opera, she'll still follow the old rule. The donation songs still have to come to the theater. So, right when it's getting good, the solicitation ticket will come again. It would be best to tell her mother that day that no matter who comes to ask for donation songs, they don't have to come. Just tell the two of them to take their place." Ruiyun said, "It doesn't matter. If they write out that they want me to go, they'll still come." Zuo Shichen said, "It doesn't matter. When the time comes, I guarantee that no one will come. I'll let you watch from beginning to end without being disturbed. Ruiyun said, "Really? If that's the case, I'll really have to thank you. But how do I tell my mother? I'm afraid she won't agree." Zuo Shichen said, "You don't have to worry about it. I have a way. It's a secret. I can't tell you in advance. When the time comes, I'll make sure you can watch the opera in peace."

Grains: Increased Supply in the Hexia Rice Market 243

General Market Still Tight

Zhabei: Yesterday, the number of boats arriving at various wharves increased, numbering around 40. Sales were very brisk. After days of quiet, shops saw a good supply and rushed to buy. The market remained tight. However, high-quality goods stabilized. Top-grade northern japonica rice inevitably had some behind-the-scenes price adjustments. Mid-range goods were slightly firmer at their original levels. As for lower-quality goods, they stood very firm. Judging from the day's situation, japonica rice may fluctuate slightly. The reason for the rise is that after the river channels opened, incoming goods could barely meet demand. However, prices are also unlikely to fall due to cost factors. Arrivals of thin indica rice were scarce, and demand was weak. Prices remained unchanged. However, high-quality goods had reached 19 yuan outside the customs. Sheep's belly glutinous rice from Hexia was being received in small quantities. Sales on this street were quite active, and prices rose slightly. Sales of Baiyuan rice were also active, but with more goods available, there were neither gains nor losses.

Hunan: Over ten boats arrived from Hexia. The market for thin indica and early rice from the southern region, such as Jinze, Fengjing, and Liantang, remained strong. This was mainly due to the scarcity of stock and the active interest of shops. Prices were tightening, but the rise in these goods in the previous few markets had been excessive, so although sales were strong yesterday, transactions decreased slightly. Because the price of Yangbu glutinous rice was approaching the price of foreign rice, shops and merchants were mostly taking a wait-and-see approach, with only sporadic transactions. Market prices were firm. Tongbian Yinyuan rice also followed suit and rose. Sales in the market felt very flat.

Reversal After High Prices of Foreign Rice 244

Spot Prices Fall Slightly by 10-20 Cents

Yesterday, two ships of foreign rice arrived. Because sales were weak and some mainland merchants were returning goods, and merchants on this street were also observing due to the arrival of goods for sale, only 4,000 bags were traded in the overall market. Prices fell slightly by 10-20 cents. The reason for the sudden and drastic changes in the market is that many ships had arrived in recent days, and foreign merchants had long been selling forward contracts. Now that these contracts were being fulfilled one after another, there was little concern for the spot goods on the market. Secondly, robberies were frequently occurring on roads in various regions, and distant mainland merchants also had concerns. Thirdly, after market prices rose repeatedly, everyone had a sense of high risk. Once there was a surge in arrivals, a reversal occurred. Over 2,000 tons of forward contracts were traded, and prices also fell slightly.

Bleached cloth was also quite active due to the sales season.

Silk and Tea: Chinese and Foreign Thrown Silk Contract Has Been Revised 248

In the local Shanghai Chinese and foreign raw silk trade, there was originally a contract for thrown silk futures, which had been mutually adhered to for a long time. However, Chinese silk merchants had suffered considerable losses over the decades due to the restrictions of the contract's terms. Taking advantage of the reorganization of the foreign merchants' silk association into an export silk association (because the contract was signed between Chinese merchants and the foreign merchants' silk association), they requested revisions. Now, the two most important clauses have been mutually negotiated and revised: (1) The payment for silk shipped on Saturdays will be made on the morning of that day, without having to wait until the following Monday to make the payment; (2) For every five pieces of silk, only two strands of sample silk are allowed to be drawn for inspection, and restrictions are shown to prevent arbitrary drawing. The sample silk must also be given a receipt. After inspection, the Chinese merchant will take the receipt to the foreign firm to retrieve it, and weigh its weight in person to avoid damage. The new revised clauses have been implemented as of yesterday (April 1st).

Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign firm silk market reported another continued increase. Yesterday, Landale & Clark and others purchased 90 bales of Shanghai white silk, and Xinfu and others purchased 12 bales of yellow reeling silk. Prices all increased sharply by 5-10 taels.

Therefore, people are panicked, and there is a great concern about loosening the standard.
