Automotive News

Special Article

A History of General Motors' Development Over the Past Twenty Years: Huang Yingdai 253

In late November of last year, the American General Motors Company held a shareholder meeting on 57th Street in New York, discussing the distribution of dividends. It was said that the dividends distributed by General Motors in recent years are richer than any factory in any country in the world. Even in terms of last year's profits alone, the net profit was 150%. The dividends distributed to the shareholders amounted to 43,500,400 yuan. In addition, the bonuses for employees and the dividends for shareholders also amounted to 43,500,000 yuan. Before Christmas, the shareholders all came to the company to receive their dividends. After this news spread, people in society were all amazed. This is because General Motors has only been established for twenty years, and even eight years ago, people in general could not say for sure whether General Motors would be permanently established or would be dissolved. The establishment of General Motors occupies an important position in the American automotive industry. To trace the origin, credit must be given to W.C. Durant. When Durant was engaged in the automotive business, it was still in its infancy. People in general did not have much faith in the automotive business. Therefore, if it were not for Durant's spirit of fearless courage and tireless efforts, General Motors would not have achieved its current success. Durant had foresight. When he started, he first bought the Buick factory and devoted himself to managing and reorganizing it. In a few years, the Buick cars produced by the factory had a completely new look and were no longer as crude as in the past. At that time, the Buick factory was located in Flint, Michigan. Horse-drawn carriage bodies, automobile engines, and bicycles, as well as all parts, were manufactured. At that time, the model was just beginning to take shape, and the equipment was simple. Compared with today, it is like heaven and earth. The organization of the new factory began in 1909, only a little over twenty years ago. It has gone through many twists and turns. It was not until eight years ago that the vehicles produced began to become popular around the world.

Durant handled all matters in the factory in an orderly manner and managed them well. All who knew him admired him. He was someone who enjoyed investing and also had new ideas. From 1905 to 1910, Durant devoted all his efforts to managing the Buick factory. After that, he entered General Motors. In 1910, General Motors' annual sales were 50,000,000 yuan, with a net profit of 10,000,000 yuan. During the war, General Motors' business developed greatly due to special circumstances. In 1917, the value of vehicles sold throughout the year reached 172,000,000 yuan. After that, it flourished day by day and developed year by year. In 1918, it was 270,000,000 yuan, and in 1920, it reached 567,000,000 yuan. However, 1921 was an unlucky year, and the company almost went bankrupt. The highest net profit in previous years was over 70,000,000 yuan. During the decline, the losses suffered were also over 38,680,000 yuan. General Motors was able to continue to exist and avoid bankruptcy because it had accumulated generous profits over the years, and its capital was so strong that it was difficult to find a large capitalist to invest in purchasing it.

After that, the company made every effort to reorganize and reform, and managed it diligently, which led to today's success. The company was able to grasp the leading position in the world's automotive business. At the beginning of General Motors' reforms, the main goal was to produce cars quickly, increase the quantity, and reform the manufacturing of parts using scientific methods. As a result, sales increased rapidly. The reason why General Motors has achieved today's success is not because of its strong capital or the large number of its factories. The main reason is that it used people properly. Most of the employees used in the various factories have rich knowledge, sufficient experience, and the ability to handle affairs is unmatched by the employees of any factory. Therefore, they are able to use scientific methods to reform the old machines and adopt new machines to manufacture various vehicles. As a result, the performance of the vehicles produced is better than other factories. People in society are happy to buy them, and sales have also increased greatly. General Motors' success today should be attributed to Durant. This has already been mentioned above. However, in addition to Durant, there is another person who should be mentioned to the readers, namely Alfred P. Sloan Jr. Since 1920, he has been the manager of General Motors. He graduated from a university in his youth. His ability to handle affairs is no less than Durant's. Therefore, these two are the cornerstones of General Motors.

When General Motors was founded, up to 1909, the value of vehicles sold in twelve months was 29,000,000 yuan, and the net profit was 9,000,000 yuan. At that time, people in the automotive industry did not believe that after that, the vehicles sold by General Motors would exceed 29,000,000 yuan. However, today's sales volume, even in the last three months of last year, is forty times the annual volume of 1909. General Motors has only been established for a little over twenty years. This has already been mentioned above. However, in these twenty years, its progress has been faster than we expected. To date, its capital is abundant and its power is great, with no match. In terms of capital, it currently has 1,200,000 US dollars. The number of employees in the factory has also reached 2,000,000. The annual production of trucks and buses has reached 2,000,000 vehicles. How could this have been foreseen by people twenty years ago? Moreover, General Motors' engineering has always had surprising and successful points, such as the abolition of horsepower and the use of gasoline, and the adoption of current systems, all of which were first invented. It is because of this that it has been able to enjoy fame to this day.

Since 1921, General Motors' business has grown even faster. In 1923, the total value of vehicles sold throughout the year was 700,000,000 yuan, and in 1926, it reached 1,000,000,000 yuan. In 1927, it was 1,269,519,673 yuan. As for last year's sales, they were even more alarming. In the previous nine months alone, the number of vehicles sold was 1,600,000, including trucks and buses. If accurate statistics are used, then in the entire United States, including women and children, General Motors sold one car for every 75 people in nine months. Until the year before last, General Motors' products accounted for one-third of all cars in the United States. Currently, the number of employees employed in the factory has reached 210,000, which is not far from the number of workers used by the American Iron and Steel Company, the Pennsylvania Railroad, and the American Telephone and Telegraph Company. The total number of workers employed by the above-mentioned four major factories has reached 1,000,000. In addition, General Motors' agents currently number 20,000. In recent years, General Motors has developed so rapidly, and its position has become increasingly stable. The main reason for the recent rapid progress of the automotive business in the United States is the increase in population, and most families have two cars. In addition, the damage of old cars and the purchase of new cars also increase sales. Generally, a car is no longer usable after seven and a half years. The development of overseas trade in recent years has also increased General Motors' sales. According to historical records, the value of General Motors' cars exported in 1926 was 98,000,000 yuan, and in 1927, it was 172,000,000 yuan. As for last year's overseas trade, according to General Motors' prior estimates, it should be 260,000,000 yuan. This number is equal to the total number of cars produced by General Motors in the years before 1918.

General Motors' factories are located in various countries around the world. Including the merchants who sell them, there are currently 6,000 locations. Its influence has reached more than 100 countries. Therefore, the development of overseas sales is due to the large number of factories and managers. Moreover, General Motors' vehicles are not shipped directly as assembled cars. They are mostly assembled by local factories. General Motors has recently discovered that it is more economical to assemble vehicles abroad, and the price can be slightly lower. Therefore, it decided to use the factory system. Recalling 1924, General Motors first established a factory in Copenhagen. Since then, factories have continued to be established in various places. To date, there are factories in London, Paris, Stockholm, Antwerp, Berlin, Madrid, Alexandria, Buenos Aires, Sao Paulo, Brisbane, Wellington, Osaka, Batavia, South Africa, and other places. Therefore, car sales have not yet reached China, Japan, India, and other eastern countries. General Motors' vehicles can also be seen everywhere. In fact, whether it is in high plateaus or low swamps, deep mountains or secluded valleys, General Motors' cars can be found almost everywhere. Although people of all colors speak different languages, their faith in General Motors' cars is the same. Therefore, General Motors' automotive business still has endless hopes. Let us wait and see.

Methods for Railroad Car Switching on the Pinghan Railway (Continued) by Zheng Baozhao 254

Next, let's discuss the railways of other countries.

Aside from England and America, other countries that implement the train dispatching system include all of the Norwegian & Swedish State Railways, major Belgian State Railways, the French Eastern Railway, the Paris-Lyons-Mediterranean Railway, and the Paris-Orleans Railway, as well as the Madri-Sarayas-slaicante Railway in Spain. What is noteworthy is that the dispatchers of the Madri-Sarayas-slaicante Railway do not participate in any train operation matters. Their primary duty is to manage the dispatch of freight cars to ensure the complete transportation of goods. When necessary, they can order the operation of auxiliary trains and pay attention to preparing the locomotives and personnel needed for these trains. In other European railways, the system can be divided into two categories: (1) The dispatching office is the sole authority for dispatching the entire section of operation. (2) The dispatching office is an organ for transmitting information. Under the first system, the sole duties of the dispatcher are as follows: (A) Before the train is assembled, determine whether it is necessary to operate auxiliary trains or special trains, considering the conditions at the originating and destination stations, the availability of motive power, and the best way to utilize motive power. Ensure that the route selected for the auxiliary train and special train does not conflict with regular trains or other trains already running on the route. After deciding to operate a train, notify the relevant stations and locomotive depots so that they can prepare the necessary locomotives and personnel in a timely manner. (2) After the train is running, if it is a double-track line, decide on switching matters or change the order of trains. If it is a single-track line, decide on the location of meeting or overtaking trains, and order the relevant stations to implement it. In case of an accident, dispatch rescue trains and arrange their itinerary. If it is a double-track line and there is an obstruction, arrange temporary single-track operation procedures. Under the second system, when the dispatching office is considered an organ for transmitting information, the decision to operate trains and various necessary arrangements after the train is running are no different from railways that do not implement a dispatching system. Railways that apply the first system include the Swedish State Railways, the Norwegian State Railways, and the Czechoslovak State Railways. As for the Paris-Orleans Railway in France, the authority of its dispatchers after the train is running is also the same. The scope of the train dispatching system in other countries' railways is generally between the first and second types. A special feature of the Belgian railway dispatching system is that the dispatcher has the right to advance the departure of freight trains when transportation conditions permit. This measure is to avoid route congestion. In addition to managing the actual operation of trains, dispatchers also handle part of the vehicle allocation matters, either as an intermediary organ between the vehicle allocation room and the station, or as the vehicle allocation organ. The dispatching office of the Belgian State Railways has a high position, with the power to manage the operation affairs of the entire line, and is directly linked to the dispatching offices of each section. All matters related to operation, such as the occurrence of any events in assembling trains and exchanging yards, as well as the waiting status of freight cars, are reported.

From the above concise description, it can be seen that the trend of world railways adopting the train dispatching system and the differences and similarities in their systems. The conclusions obtained from a comprehensive comparison and observation of various countries' systems, as well as the consideration of our country's situation, and the specific methods considered for reference and adoption, have been fully documented in this plan. It is not necessary to repeat them here. What has not been discussed in detail in the plan is specifically stated in the following points for further explanation:

(1) Organization: The centralized system and the sectionalized system each have their advantages. Which type is more advantageous for each road depends on the management system, the length of the route, and the complexity of transportation. Generally speaking, the centralized system enables the entire road to comprehensively coordinate all transportation affairs. Therefore, it is easier to achieve effectiveness in considering the transportation situation of each section, allocating vehicles, and utilizing locomotive capacity, etc. The routes of the British railways are shorter than those of various countries and territories, so the centralized system is quite suitable. Most of the routes in the United States are widely spread and mostly involve large-volume freight transport, so it is necessary to adopt the sectionalized system. Most of our country's major routes span two or three provinces in length. In terms of topography, the sectionalized system is more suitable. However, the transportation of various roads is far less heavy than that of European and American railways. Therefore, the organizational system should be simple and economical. Due to the lack of talent, the centralized system can concentrate the operation affairs of the entire road in the hands of a relatively small number of people. Therefore, within the possible scope, the centralized system should be adopted.

(2) Dedicated Telephone: The operation of the train dispatching system should be equipped with a complete dedicated telephone as an indispensable tool.

The transmission of information and the issuing of orders require speed. Even a slight delay can negate its effectiveness. Railways in Sweden, Norway, Belgium, Spain, and France are mostly equipped with selective telephones. The plan for the installation of dedicated telephones on the Pinghan Railway is appended later for reference.

(3) Vehicle Allocation: Vehicle allocation is either handled concurrently by the dispatching office, such as on the London Midland Railway, or handled by a separate organization, such as on the London and North Eastern Railway. However, the Midland Railway alone has more than 128,000 freight cars, with no less than a hundred types. In our country, the total number of freight cars on all railways combined is only over 17,000. The largest number of freight cars on major roads is no more than three or four thousand. The disparity in the complexity of affairs is more than several dozen times. Therefore, it is believed that the dispatching office can competently handle vehicle allocation matters concurrently.

(4) Dispatching of Locomotives and Train Crews: Since the train guards belong to the car service personnel, they should be under the management of the car service. As for the rotation and dispatch of other workers such as drivers and firemen, as well as the allocation and command of locomotives, they are either under the management of the car service or the locomotive service. The railways of various countries differ due to different organizations. However, since these affairs are considerably related to train dispatching, they should be managed concurrently by one leader, which will easily achieve effectiveness. The future trend of railways in various countries will inevitably lean towards this type of organization. Although this differs from the current system of dividing the duties of the car and locomotive departments in our country's railways, we should judge whether it is sound in principle and appropriate in practice. Therefore, this plan holds this view on locomotive service matters, in order to show the intention of striving for reform and not being bound by the current system.

Finally, the author has one more thing to say. Professor E.R. Sherrngton of Transportation Studies at the University of London once revealed the essence of the train dispatching system, saying, "This system lies in concentrating the dispatch of trains in the hands of a relatively small number of personnel with high-level training and high salaries, and also enabling them to have a clear understanding of the entire line of transportation under their jurisdiction." Therefore, even with good laws and good intentions, it is especially important to have personnel who can implement them and be good at using them. Zhuangzi said that the medicine for preventing chapped hands is the same, but some use it to dominate, while others cannot avoid making a living by washing silk floss generation after generation. This depends on the self-improvement of all those in the national railway industry. The creation of this humble plan is of negligible benefit. (The End)

Peisheng Company Sells Yijincao: Peisheng Pharmaceutical Company at No. 203 Zhonghua Road, Southern City, announced that the secret recipe Yijincao issued by the company is effective for treating pulmonary tuberculosis, hemoptysis and other diseases, and can cure the root cause without recurrence after recovery. The price is extremely low, one yuan and two dimes per dose, and six yuan for half a dozen.

News from Outside the Realm 260

The Third Issue of Honeycomb Pictorial is Published: The Honeycomb Society announced that the Honeycomb Pictorial is a publication issued by the society, finely printed with live block letters, with a beautiful form and rich content, and is indeed the only publication of modern Chinese art. It has been published with each issue, and the third issue has now been published. The printed pictures are extremely valuable, and the texts are mostly anecdotes of celebrities, which are quite interesting. This newspaper has newspapers for sale, and those who subscribe for the whole year can go to the clubhouse at No. 158 Wangping Street or No. 92 Pingle Lane on Xizang Road to pay the money. The whole year only costs one yuan.

The Journal of the Chinese Institute of Engineers, Volume 5, Issue 2, is Published: The Chinese Institute of Engineers at No. 7 Ningbo Road announced that the association is the only organization of engineers in our country. It has been established for more than ten years. In addition to researching academic studies and subsidizing construction, it also publishes a journal called Engineering. The most recently published one is Volume 5, Issue 2, which includes major items such as Ling Hongxun's "General Overview of the Construction of the Longhai Railway and the Progress of New Work", Zhang Xueyang's "The Greeves-Tcheou Method of Indirect Alkalization for Soap Making", Song Xishang's "New Method of Protecting River Banks (English)", Lu Junhe's "Discussion on the Provisions of Gun Barrel Materials", Li Shutian's "The Status Quo and Preliminary Plan of the Northern Great Port", the editor's "Engineering and Accounting (English)", Shi Chongzhi's "Study Notes on the Anaconde Steel Works in England (English)", Fan Benzhong's "The General Situation of the Shanghai Wireless Telegraph Bureau in the Era of the Construction Commission", Wei Daming's "Aviation and Radio", Zhu Ruijie's "New Plan for Steam Turbine Power Plants", etc. Other sections such as the communication column and the improvement column have extremely wonderful works. The price is three dimes per copy, one yuan and eight fen for the whole year in this city, and one yuan and two jiao for other places. The books are sold at the association's headquarters, or at the Commercial Press, Minzhi Bookstore, Ximendong New Bookstore, Xujiahui Suxin Bookstore, etc.

Road Association Publishes Lu Shi: The China National Road Construction Association announced that this year is the 10th anniversary of the association. Experts are invited to translate and write many books to serve research. The first is in the city Construction Science, the real price is eight angles, the deposit is five angles, the second is Yang Zhuming's Bridge Engineering, the real price per book is two yuan, the deposit is one yuan and five angles (the deposit deadline is the end of April), and the third is the five-angle road introduction of the yellow article. , are added with postage, the book has been printed, and it will be published next month.
